# Toras Menachem Vol 04

Toras Menachem

## – 4 – Year 5712 – Part One

## Title Page

### Title Page

Farbrengens
(Monday of Rosh Hashanah - Shabbos Parshas Mishpatim, Mevarchim HaChodesh Adar)

## B’s”d. The Second Day of Rosh Hashanah, 5712

(An unedited transcript)

(In a maamar of the Alter Rebbe, recorded by R’ P., it is stated:)
"They shall speak of the glory of Your kingdom and talk of Your power, to make known to the sons of man His mighty acts," etc.. The primary structure of *Malchus* is built from the *Gevuros*. That is to say, for it to be possible for the *Ohr Ein Sof* to exist within the worlds of *Beriah, Yetzirah,* and *Asiyah*—the worlds of separation—there must be concealments and *Tzimtzumim*. For in the realm of *Atzilus*, "He and His attributes are one", similar to the powers of the soul that extend into the limbs of the body, etc. Likewise, in the realm of *Atzilus*, even the *keilim* (vessels) are all aspects of *Elokus*. However, in the worlds of *Beriah, Yetzirah,* and *Asiyah*—the world of separation—even the angels, "the host of heaven bows down to You", are nevertheless considered an entity of *yesh* and separation, a thing external that possesses free choice. [This is a novel point, for it is explicit in *Tanya* that angels do not possess free choice, yet here it is explained that they do, and proof is brought for this from the fact that "they expelled Metatron", etc.] Therefore, there must first be a structure built from *Gevurah* so that later, through concealments and *Tzimtzumim*, the worlds of *Beriah, Yetzirah,* and *Asiyah* can come into being; for if not, everything would be in the state of *Ein Sof*, etc. Yet, if the *Gevuros* were not sweetened, it would be possible for there to be total separation. Therefore, "Avraham established the throne", and through the sweetening of the *Gevuros*, there can be *bitul* in the world of separation—"the host of heaven bows down to You."

"At the beginning of the King’s decree, He carved", etc.—it arose in His simple will that there should be a dwelling place in the lower worlds. But after this, it must be brought about through the elevation of *mayin nukvin* (feminine waters) so that He may derive *taanug* (pleasure) from the *bitul* of the created beings, before whom "everything is considered as nothing". How can He receive *taanug* from them? It is like the *bitul* of a fly, which is incomparable, etc. Everything was brought into being through many *Tzimtzumim* from Him in the *Seder Hishtalshelus*, etc. Therefore, there must be an *is'arusa d'letata* (arousal from below) to draw down the aspect of *taanug*, as it is written, "Then you shall delight in Hashem".

Now, on Rosh Hashanah—"this day is the beginning of Your works" —when things return to their source, one must draw down as mentioned above. This is the meaning of "reciting *Malchiyos* before Him", similar to "And Hashem has exalted you today" —a term of glorification, like bringing an object before a king and praising it before him in order to draw forth from the King that He should derive *taanug* from this object. This is the meaning of "From generation to generation, make Him King," etc., "for He alone is exalted and holy". Therefore, one must draw down that He should derive *taanug* from the aspect of *Malchus*, etc. This is the meaning of the three *Uv'chein* —all of the above.

One must understand: if so, on the night of Rosh Hashanah, before the drawing down mentioned above via *Malchiyos*, etc., from where does the world derive its existence? But it is known that in every thing there is an internal and an external aspect, just as we see in thought, speech, and action, where the powers of the soul extend into each. However, the soul-power in speech is more internal than the soul-power in action, and likewise, the soul-power in thought is more internal than the soul-power in speech. Nevertheless, each is comprised of everything—that is, *Chochma, Binah, Da’as, Chesed, Gevurah, Tiferes, Netzach, Hod, Yesod, Malchus*—as we see that in action there is also intellect, etc. It is just that one is the aspect of *pnimiyus* (internality) and the other is the aspect of *chitzoniyus* (externality), etc. Likewise, in the creation of the worlds—that is, in the aspect of *Malchus*—there are all the *Sefiros* as mentioned above. Therefore, the angels who receive from the aspect of *Malchus* have comprehension and derive pleasure from the *ziv* (radiance), etc., "six wings", etc., and all the more so the *neshamos*. [It may be said that what is stated, "they have comprehension and derive pleasure," etc., "six wings," etc., corresponds to *Chochma, Binah, Da’as* and *Chesed, Gevurah, Tiferes, Netzach, Hod, Yesod* as mentioned above; for comprehension and pleasure from the *ziv* is the matter of *Chochma, Binah, Da’as*, and the six wings are the *middos* of *Chesed, Gevurah, Tiferes, Netzach, Hod, Yesod*.]

*Malchus* receives *hashpa'ah* (influence) from *Ze'er Anpin*, and there are two modes in this: the aspect of *panim b'panim* (face-to-face), where *Malchus* receives from the *pnimiyus* of *Ze'er Anpin*, etc., and the aspect of *achor b'achor* (back-to-back). It is like one who receives a concept of wisdom from the mouth of the wise man himself (which is the aspect of *panim b'panim*), while others receive from the aspect of the "back" through the aspect of *Netzach, Hod, Yesod*. It is like receiving wisdom from a written text; even though the wisdom is clothed in the text, the reception is from the aspect of the "back" through the aspect of *Netzach, Hod, Yesod* (or even lower, the aspect of *Asiyah*), [especially since the recipient also receives through his own aspect of *Netzach, Hod, Yesod*].

Now, on Rosh Hashanah, "in the covering for the day of our festival". It is like a king who, wishing to instill awe, hides himself. The existence of all the worlds is only through the *kista d'chiyusa* (the spark of vitality), and it receives from the aspect of *Netzach, Hod, Yesod*—the aspect of "back." There are those who receive only from the aspect of *Netzach, Hod, Yesod*, and then it is called *achor b'achor*. When *Malchus* is in joy, it is in a state of revelation and makes a feast, etc., and then it is called "Your right hand shall embrace me" on the festival of Sukkos, etc. Therefore, on Rosh Hashanah, one must call to the King that He should turn His face to us and draw down *taanug* from the Source of all *taanugim* through the verses of Torah—"Torah emanates from *Chochma*" and its root is above the aspect of *Keter*, the aspect of *Atik*, etc. But this alone is not enough, for *Malchus* is the aspect of speech—"By the word of Hashem were the heavens made" —and "a prisoner cannot free himself". Therefore, there must also be the *shofar*—that is, the *tekiah*, a simple sound, the *re'usa d'liba* (desire of the heart) from the hiddenness of the heart to revelation, and "spirit brings spirit and draws forth spirit" from the hidden to the revealed, from the aspect of *ratzon* (will), etc.

And specifically through the *shofar*. As is known, there are the categories of *domem* (inanimate), *tzomei'ach* (vegetative), *chai* (animate), and *medaber* (speaking). The *domem* is the lowest level, yet the *tzomei'ach* receives from the *domem*, the *chai* is nourished by the *tzomei'ach*, and the *medaber* from the *chai*, as is known, etc. This is because in its root, the *domem* is from the highest level of all—the aspect of the world of *Tohu*. As we see clearly in the summer, the revelation from *ayin* (nothingness) to *yesh* (being) comes specifically from the aspect of *domem*, from which all grasses and trees grow, for that which is highest of all can descend the furthest, etc. In man, there is the aspect of *tikkun*—that is, the *Nefesh Elokis* within him, the aspect of *Mah* that clarifies—and he also has the aspect of *nogah*, called the *tzelem* (image), etc., which is clarified. Therefore, when the Beis Hamikdash existed, "there is no joy except with meat" —the aspect of *chai*—because when the aspect of *nogah* is clarified, there is joy, for in its root it is higher, etc. Therefore, through the *shofar*, one can draw down the aspect of *taanug*, etc., from the Source of *taanug*—"Improve your deeds", etc. Through man and the *shofar*, which clarifies and is clarified, the elevation of *mayin nukvin* from *Tohu* and *Tikkun* draws down as mentioned above. This is "in your mouth and in your heart", etc. However, through the *tekiah* alone—that is, drawing down a simple sound from the Supernal Source—the created beings would not be able to receive the "Fear of Yitzchak", etc., just as when He extended His finger among them and burned them through the revelation of the *Ohr Haganuz* (Hidden Light) that exceeded their capacity to receive. There are angels that are created every day and then cease to exist; this is "He causes the grass to grow for the cattle", "He swallows them in one gulp" through the revelation of light as mentioned above. And there are angels called "the standing acacia trees", etc., and this is "He creates ministers and His ministers", etc. And when the revelation comes in the future, it is written, "And they shall enter the caves of the rocks," etc., "from the fear," etc. Therefore, the *shevarim* are for breaking the strength—this is "You have shattered with Your might", etc., to be in the state of shattering. And the *teruah* is a wailing cry to arouse mercy from the Thirteen Attributes, etc. Through this, there is afterwards the final *tekiah* from above to below, so that everything will be in a state of *ratzo v'shov* (running and returning).

Now, all that was explained above in the maamar of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe concerns the *Malchus* of *Atzilus*, etc. But in truth, it is the same in the levels within *Malchus* that are infinitely higher, up to the *Malchus* of *Ein Sof*. For what was explained regarding the removal and elevation of *Malchus* on Rosh Hashanah does not mean mere inclusion and concealment, but total removal. As explained in the *drushim* of the Rebbe Rayatz (in the *hemshechim* of Rosh Hashanah), the removal of the *Sefirah* of *Malchus* on Rosh Hashanah is an aspect of concealment that is not in existence (which is not at all like the concealment that exists within existence); that is, *Malchus* ascends to a level that is not in existence at all. From this, it is understood that this matter is not only in the *Malchus* of *Atzilus* but in all levels of *Malchus*, up to the aspect of *Malchus* of *Ein Sof*. According to this, it is even more difficult to understand why this matter of Rosh Hashanah is specifically on the sixth day of creation, the day Adam HaRishon was created, and not on the 25th of Elul, when the entire world was created. For if the elevation of *Malchus* on Rosh Hashanah were only a matter of concealment and inclusion, the connection to the day of Adam HaRishon’s creation would be understood. But since the removal is such that it returns entirely to its source, as mentioned above from the Alter Rebbe’s maamar, that one must arouse the will anew, then this should have been on the first day of creation, the 25th of Elul, when the formation of all created beings *yesh me'ayin* (being from nothingness) took place. Whereas on the sixth day of creation, there was only the formation of the body of Adam HaRishon and the blowing of a soul into his nostrils, for the souls already existed before that, and even before the creation of all created beings, as the saying goes, "The thought of Yisrael preceded everything." If so, it is wondrous why this day was fixed specifically as Rosh Hashanah, on which all things return to their source, etc.

But the matter is as follows: it is explained in the Alter Rebbe’s maamar there that the purpose of creation is that Hashem desired to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds. Why He desired this, we do not know, and as it is explained, "For a desire, there is no reason." But this we do know: the reason for creation is that Hashem desired to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds. With this, we can understand the novelty of the sixth day of creation, for the beginning of the fulfillment of the intent of a "dwelling place in the lower worlds" was on the sixth day of creation, the day Adam HaRishon was created. For the soul is a "part of Hashem from above" truly, and "he who blows, blows from within himself"—from His internality and essence. And the body is physical and created as a vessel, and as is known, the manner of his creation is not like the creation of the bodies of other living creatures. And if so, the connection of the soul, which is a "part of Hashem from above" truly, with the body, which is physical, is the matter of a "dwelling place in the lower worlds." Therefore, Rosh Hashanah was fixed on the sixth day of creation specifically, and not on the 25th of Elul, because on the sixth day of creation, the day Adam HaRishon was created, the fulfillment of the intent of creation—that Hashem desired to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds—was initiated. This is also why this day affects the created beings that were created before Adam HaRishon, for before the creation of Adam HaRishon, there was only an external influence, of which it is written, "By the word of Hashem were the heavens made," which is the aspect of *chitzoniyus*. But with the creation of Adam HaRishon, there was an internal influence from above—"He blew from within Himself"—and this brought about the fulfillment of the intent in all created beings: that Hashem desired to have a dwelling place in the lower worlds. Therefore, the day of Rosh Hashanah was fixed on the day of Adam HaRishon’s creation specifically, because that is the ultimate intent of the "dwelling place in the lower worlds"—that the internal light should shine in the externality of the world, and below ten *tefachim*, for a good and sweet year in goodness that is seen and revealed.

## Sicha of the Second Day of Rosh Hashanah 5712

**A.** [The Rebbe washed his holy hands for the meal and instructed the entire congregation to wash their hands for the meal, saying:]
I wish—despite the difficulty in instituting a new practice that I did not see from my father-in-law, the Rebbe—to hold a Yom Tov meal, with Birchas Hamazon and a Kos Shel Bracha, together with the entire congregation. Therefore, it is appropriate that the entire congregation wash their hands for the meal, sing the Nigun of the Alter Rebbe, and afterwards recite Birchas Hamazon with a Kos Shel Bracha.
[The Rebbe distributed pieces of his challah to those present.]

*

**B.** It is explained in the discourses of Chassidus that every Rosh Hashanah eve (night), the vitality (of the previous year) ascends to its root and source. Through the blowing of the Shofar and the prayers, a new light is drawn down—a light that is higher, one that had not yet shone since the days of old.
[Based on this, we can understand the verse, "From the beginning of the year to the end of the year"—which seemingly is difficult, for at the end of this year, the next year begins, and thus it should have said "forever." The explanation is that "each and every year there is a new, higher light, for the light that was renewed and shone on this Rosh Hashanah ascends on the eve of the coming Rosh Hashanah to its source, and that is the meaning of 'from the beginning of the year to the end of the year' alone."]
One can bring an example of this from the order of avodah every single day:
At the end of the day, in Krias Shema Al Hamitah, one must conduct an accounting of the entire day. Afterwards, during sleep, the soul (the vitality) departs and ascends on high [and those who are worthy achieve insights in Torah as their souls ascend to the supernal chambers, each according to the level of his avodah during the day], and through this, it draws life for the sake of the renewal of vitality when one wakes from his sleep and becomes a "new creation."
Similarly, every year—regarding the general vitality of the entire year—at the end of the year (on the eve and night of Rosh Hashanah until the blowing of the Shofar), the vitality of the previous year departs (and therefore one must conduct an accounting of the entire year), and afterwards, a new, higher light is drawn down.
It can be said that just as at the time of the renewal of vitality each day we recite ("Modeh Ani... that You have returned my soul within me," and following that) the eighteen morning blessings, so too regarding the renewal of vitality on Rosh Hashanah through the Shofar blowing and the prayers—the Sages instituted nine blessings in the Mussaf of Rosh Hashanah and nine blasts, which total eighteen, corresponding to the eighteen morning blessings.

**C.** More specifically, the renewal of vitality on Rosh Hashanah is both regarding the general vitality of the entire year and regarding the specific vitality of this day:
To preface with a question in the revealed Torah: Seemingly, it is not understood why we recite the morning blessings on the morning of the second day of Rosh Hashanah. After all, "the two days of Rosh Hashanah... are considered as one long day," "like one long day." If so, why should the night's sleep not be considered like sleep in the middle of a "long day," after which one does not recite the morning blessings?!
The explanation for this:
On Rosh Hashanah there are two aspects: (1) A "head" for all the days of the year (similar to the "head" for all the limbs of the body), which contains the general vitality of the entire year; (2) In addition to this, it is also one of the days of the year, like any specific day, which has the specific vitality belonging to this day (just as the "head" is also one of the limbs of the body).
Therefore: The fact that the two days of Rosh Hashanah are considered a "long day" applies only to the general vitality of the entire year. But regarding the specific vitality, the second day of Rosh Hashanah is considered a day unto itself, and for this reason, one is obligated to recite the morning blessings on it as on every other day.

**D.** One should add to the comparison of the renewal of vitality on Rosh Hashanah to the renewal of vitality each day, which is expressed in the recitation of the morning blessings:
The obligation of the morning blessings is for *everyone*, even for one who was not obligated in one or several of them—meaning, he did not feel the renewal of vitality in that specific matter. Nevertheless, he is obligated to bless for the renewal of vitality in all matters, for "all the blessings are on the order of the world and its conduct... that Hashem created the needs of the world."
Likewise, regarding the renewal of vitality on Rosh Hashanah—all the influences and revelations, even regarding physical matters, children, life, and ample sustenance "below ten handbreadths," are drawn down *for everyone*. Even one who did not feel the influences of Rosh Hashanah within himself must know that all the influences were drawn down, and the matter depends only on him—"he must open his ear-tube" (listening tube), and then he will feel the influences within himself.
[The Rebbe instructed to play the "Rosh Hashanah melody," and afterwards instructed to play the Alter Rebbe’s Nigun of Four Parts.]

***

**E.** The Mitteler Rebbe explains in *Shaar HaTeki'os* that "the essence of the influence in an abundance of light and vitality is only through the aspect of *Gevuros* specifically (the Gevurah of Yitzchak), because they contain a *greater intensity of light and vitality* with more immense power than the power of Chasadim... and this is what we find, that the essence and source of all blessings for the world was drawn by Yitzchak specifically, and we do not find such a matter of blessings for Avraham or Yaakov... because from him specifically is the source of blessings..."
[He continues to explain that "the reason Yitzchak did not want to bless Yaakov but rather Eisav is because the aspect of Gevurah of Eisav is in the 'waste' of the Gevuros of Yitzchak, and according to Yitzchak’s opinion, they would not be clarified now if not through the blessings," and he concludes that "Yaakov, who wore the garments of Eisav, drew down the blessing so that the sparks would be clarified in Asiyah now, and the time of clarification would not be so long, and Mashiach will come speedily, Amen."]
"However, from another perspective, the aspect of Gevuros is not good, because they are in the aspect of *ascent and inclusion* on high," "the aspect of fear and awe in the aspect of ascent on high, and not to descend and be drawn below at all." Therefore, "one must draw them below through the power of Chasadim *that sweetens them*, and this is through the aspect of Yaakov who sweetens Yitzchak through the aspect of the Chasadim of Avraham." And "this is also the root of the matter of the blowing of the Shofar, which is 'a groaning groan... in Shevarim and Teruah,' to break and sweeten the aspect of Gevuros... the aspect of Yitzchak... through Yaakov who redeemed Avraham... as it is written in the Zohar that Yaakov and Avraham are unified in Yitzchak... to sweeten the Gevuros within him."
[One should add and explain the connection of the sweetening of the Gevuros to Shevarim and Teruah, the groaning and wailing—that this is similar to what we see physically in a person who is suffering greatly, who groans and wails, where the groaning and wailing itself causes him a certain relief.]
Similarly, it is explained in a Maamar of the Alter Rebbe, the notes of R. P., regarding the general matter of creation through the Sefirah of Malchus (whose building is on Rosh Hashanah)—that "the essence of the building of Malchus is from *Gevurah*, meaning, that for it to be possible for there to be from the aspect of Ein Sof into the worlds of BYA, which are separate worlds, there must be concealments and Tzimtzumim, for in the aspect of Atzilus, 'He and His attributes are one'... therefore there must first be its building from Gevurah so that afterwards, through concealments and Tzimtzumim, it can be BYA. For otherwise, everything would be in the aspect of Ein Sof. However, if the Gevuros were not sweetened, it could be completely separate, therefore 'Avraham established the throne,' and through the Gevuros being *sweetened*, there can be Bitul in the world of the separate entities."
[It should be noted that in the aforementioned Maamar, it was explained only regarding Malchus of Atzilus, but in truth, it is so even higher, up to Malchus of Ein Sof, and regarding this it is said, "From generation to generation You have made Him King," the double mention of "generation," which can be said (similar to the interpretation of the Tzemach Tzedek on this matter) refers to Malchus of Atzilus and Malchus of Ein Sof.]
One should add that the matter of the sweetening of the Gevuros [for the sake of the influence in the world] in the avodah of the human soul is the matter of Teshuvah, which must be for each person according to his situation, as the saying of the Rebbe Maharash—which they said in a Maamar of Rosh Hashanah—that even a perfectly righteous person who is distracted from Torah study due to physical weakness must do Teshuvah from the depths of the heart (as has already been printed in a Sicha of the Rebbe).

**F.** (The Rebbe concluded:) And as we stand close to the conclusion of Rosh Hashanah, after the blowing of the Shofar, the avodah of Teshuvah, etc.—the influence can already be drawn down into the world.
One can connect this with the *recitation of Chassidus*—as the Rebbe related that his father, the Rebbe (Rashab), would be accustomed to saying a Maamar of Chassidus on the second day of Rosh Hashanah toward evening, and continue his recitation into the night ("drawing it into the night"). He explained the reason for this—in two ways: (a) that all the influences that were activated during the forty-eight hours of the two days of Rosh Hashanah should be drawn into the world, (b) that the light of Chassidus should shine in the world.
[The Rebbe instructed to play "The Beinoni." Afterwards, he recited Birchas Hamazon over the cup and gave from the Kos Shel Bracha to all those present.]

***

**G.** He instructed to play and said a Maamar beginning with the words "Kvod Malchusecha."
[Before beginning the Maamar, he said: There is a transcript by the Chassid R. Pinchas Reizes from a Maamar of the Alter Rebbe—in this transcript, the things are fragmented, and it is a matter of study whether the Maamar was said in this style, or if this transcript is only an outline—and attached to this is a note in the holy handwriting of the Tzemach Tzedek, "This discourse is the notes and manuscript of R. P. of Shklov, said on the night of Rosh Hashanah 5566," and he adds afterwards, "The discourse of my grandfather, the Rebbe, in the year 5633, beginning 'To understand the matter of the Nesirah' in the year 5605, was written from this note of R. P."]
And the beginning of the Maamar—"Kvod Malchusecha Yomru..."

***

**H.** The Rebbe related that he once entered his father, the Rebbe, the day after Yom Kippur, and asked him: What is the avodah now? And he answered him: Now, in particular, one must do Teshuvah ("Now one must first do Teshuvah").
And so it can be said in the present case—as we stand at the conclusion of Rosh Hashanah—that although certainly all the influences of Rosh Hashanah have already been drawn down, and even into the physicality of the world, nevertheless, now in particular there must be ("now there must first be") the continuation of the avodah of Rosh Hashanah—*Kabbalas Ol* (acceptance of the yoke).
And this matter is emphasized by the fact that Rosh Hashanah is included in the Ten Days of Teshuvah:
Although the implication of the language of the Gemara, "The ten days *between* Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur," is that Rosh Hashanah (and likewise Yom Kippur) is not included in the "ten days," the truth is that the count of "*ten* days" includes Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, and without Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur (the days between them), they are only seven days.
The explanation for this is similar to what was said above (section G) that on Rosh Hashanah there is general vitality and specific vitality—that there are two aspects on Rosh Hashanah: (a) its special nature that is distinct from the days that follow it, (b) its being one of the Ten Days of Teshuvah.
And from this, it is also understood regarding the matter of Kabbalas Ol:
The Kabbalas Ol of Rosh Hashanah is a *general* Kabbalas Ol, and since the intention is that the matter of Kabbalas Ol (should not remain in a surrounding manner, but) should be drawn down internally, therefore, after the general Kabbalas Ol of Rosh Hashanah, there must be a continuation of the avodah of Kabbalas Ol during the Ten Days of Teshuvah (of which Rosh Hashanah is one)—to draw the Kabbalas Ol down internally, a *specific* Kabbalas Ol regarding every single detail, in thought, speech, and action.

**I.** One should add that the Kabbalas Ol itself must be with *joy*, as it is written, "*And rejoice* with trembling," meaning, that even the nullification and Kabbalas Ol ("trembling") must be from within joy ("rejoice").
However, seemingly it is not understood:
Acceptance of the yoke of Kingship is in the ultimate nullification, to such an extent that even "a gesture in the presence of the King, etc." (is severely punished). And all the more so during the Ten Days of Teshuvah—about which it is said, "Seek Hashem when He is found, call upon Him when He is near," that at this time there is a closeness of the "Light" to the "spark"—certainly when the "*Light*" itself is found in closeness ("the Light itself is found"), this causes *ultimate nullification*, which rules out even a "gesture." If so, how is it possible that the Kabbalas Ol should be with joy, a movement of *expansion*?
The explanation for this is that this matter (that standing before the King rules out even a "gesture in the presence of the King") is only regarding a king of flesh and blood. This is not so regarding the *King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He*—He gives the possibility that standing before Him ("in the presence of the King"), in a state and situation of the closeness of the Light to the spark, can be with joy.
In the language of the prayer of the day: "Whether as children, whether as servants," meaning, we are given the choice to choose whichever way we want, what is good and preferable for us ("what is better for us"). Consequently, even if from the perspective of the feeling of "servants" there must be ultimate nullification that rules out even a "gesture" ("something that is not quite right"), from the perspective of the feeling of "children," we can ask and we do ask for all matters (not just something, "at least something"), even the most sublime matters, including also—in the present case—that the Kabbalas Ol should be with joy.

**J.** And there are two matters in this:
First and foremost—the virtue of avodah with joy, that "it is a great avodah" (as the ruling of the Rambam), that then all matters are done with vitality and alacrity, and consequently, in a more sublime and complete manner.
And another matter in this—that when the Kabbalas Ol is with joy, from the perspective of the feeling of "children," then there is an opening of a door so that he can ask of Hashem that He should forgive him even if he failed, G-d forbid, in undesirable conduct (the opposite of Kabbalas Ol).

**K.** Based on this, one can explain the order of the blessings that the Men of the Great Assembly instituted in the Mussaf of Rosh Hashanah—Malchiyos and afterwards Zichronos:
Seemingly, they should have preceded the verses of Zichronos to the verses of Malchiyos, for after the aspect of Kingship is drawn down, it is not relevant that the King should forget His people, which would involve the matter of remembrance. If so, after we say the verses of Malchiyos and conclude "Rule over the entire world in Your glory... Blessed are You, Hashem, King over all the earth"—from which it is proven clearly "without any doubt or double doubt in the world" that Hashem has become King, for otherwise, we would not bless, as "a doubtful blessing is to be avoided due to the concern of a blessing in vain"—what place is there still for the verses of Zichronos?
And among the explanations for this—in addition to the fact that the content of the verses of Zichronos is regarding the *details* of the matters of "all the works... all the creatures... to remember every spirit and soul, etc." (as all the details of the matters that we say in the blessing of Zichronos)—is that after Hashem accepts the request of Israel and becomes King, it is possible that the conduct will not be as it should be, G-d forbid, and regarding this we say the verses of Zichronos, that even in an undesirable situation, G-d forbid, Hashem should remember for them the merit of the fathers, the binding of Yitzchak, etc.
And not only that, but Hashem says to Israel, "Say before Me... Malchiyos so that you may make Me King over you; Zichronos so that your remembrance may ascend before Me for good," meaning, that from the outset He opens a door for them and informs them that even if after the acceptance of His Kingship their conduct will be undesirable, G-d forbid, they can ask and activate that their remembrance should ascend before Him for good—similar to what Hashem said to Moshe Rabbeinu, "And now, leave Me alone," "here He opened a door for him and informed him that the matter depends on him, that if he prays, He will not destroy them."

**L.** One should add regarding the matter of the joy in Kabbalas Ol in greater depth:
By way of preface—that the empowerment for the general matter of Malchiyos (that the Jewish people should be able to make Hashem King) is from the greatness of the importance and praise of Israel before Hashem, to such an extent that "the Holy One, Blessed be He, praises Himself with the praise of Israel... as it is written, 'And Hashem has exalted you (a term of importance and praise) today... I will make you one unique nation in the world, as it is said, And who is like Your people Israel, one nation on earth.'"
Based on this, one can explain what is said in the Maamar that "*Say* before Me Malchiyos so that you may make Me King over you" is like "And Hashem *exalted you* today":
Regarding the matter of "make Me King over you" (that the Jewish people make Hashem King)—it is more appropriate (seemingly) the praise *that the Jewish people praise Hashem*, as it is written in the verse before it, "You have *exalted* Hashem today." Why does the Maamar bring the verse "And Hashem *exalted you* today," which speaks about the praise *that Hashem praises Israel*?
It can be said that in this is hinted *that the empowerment* for the general matter of the saying of Malchiyos ("Say before Me Malchiyos, etc.") is from the *importance and praise of Israel*—"And Hashem exalted you today."
And since the empowerment for the general matter of the saying of Malchiyos is from the importance and praise of Israel—it is understood that the Kabbalas Ol ("make Me King over you") is not by way of compulsion, but from *joy* specifically, as stated, "Rejoice with trembling."

**M.** However, on the other hand—one should not be satisfied with joy in itself, but there must also be Kabbalas Ol, "Rejoice *with trembling*" (just as one should not be satisfied with Kabbalas Ol in itself, but there must also be joy, "*Rejoice* with trembling").
And this matter is hinted at in the Mitzvah of Tefillin:
The matter of "And Hashem exalted you today," that "the Holy One, Blessed be He, praises Himself with the praise of Israel" (from which is made the acceptance of Kingship on Rosh Hashanah through the blowing of the Shofar with *joy*)—is brought in the Gemara regarding the Mitzvah of Tefillin: "The Tefillin of the Master of the World, what is written in them? And who is like Your people Israel, one nation on earth." And from this is understood the *greatness of the joy* in the fulfillment of the Mitzvah of Tefillin.
And the content of the Mitzvah of Tefillin is the subjugation of the heart and the mind (as explained in the Shulchan Aruch and in Tanya), which is the matter of *Kabbalas Ol*. And not only that, but the Tefillin themselves are made from the skin of an animal (including also the parchments in the Tefillin which are written on parchment made from the skin of an animal), and their binding on the hand and the head (against the heart and the mind) is by straps made from the skin of an animal—*animal* specifically, in which is emphasized the matter of *nullification and Kabbalas Ol*.
It should be noted that this matter (the connection to an animal) is also emphasized in the blowing of the Shofar—that the fulfillment of the Mitzvah is through the horn of an *animal* specifically, and in the horn of an animal one blows a *plain sound* specifically, and afterwards *Shevarim Teruah* (groaning and wailing), from the language of breaking and crumbling ("to break and crumble")—that all these matters indicate and emphasize the matter of *nullification and Kabbalas Ol*.
And specifically through nullification and Kabbalas Ol, one activates all the influences of Rosh Hashanah, both in spirituality and in physicality, as the words of the Rebbe (in the name of the Alter Rebbe) that Hashem gives Jews physicality, and Jews make from the physicality spirituality.

## With the help of Hashem. Blessing of the Rebbe, Erev Yom Kippur 5712

### With the help of Hashem. Blessing of the Rebbe, Erev Yom Kippur 5712

Unedited

1. [Following Shacharis, Anash arrived to receive "lekach" from the Rebbe. He gave each person a piece of "lekach" along with his holy blessing. After midday, a group of Anash entered to request his blessing, and he said:]

May you be sealed and inscribed for good, in both material and spiritual matters.
May it be the will of Hashem that there be a true awakening of teshuvah, that Hashem accept all our prayers, and that He grant and add to each and every one everything they require.
A good and sweet year—"a gezunter yohr un a ziser yohr"—in goodness that is visible and revealed.

2. [Following Mincha, a second group of Anash entered to request his blessing, and he said:]

May you be sealed and inscribed for good.
May it be the will of Hashem that all our prayers be accepted among the prayers of all of Klal Yisroel.
May we all have a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike, in goodness that is visible and revealed.

3. [Toward evening, a third group of Anash entered to request his blessing, and he said:]

May you be sealed and inscribed for good.
May it be the will of Hashem that all prayers be accepted.
May it be a good and sweet year, "below ten tefachim," in goodness that is visible and revealed.

## With the help of Hashem. The Rebbe’s Blessing to the Students
Erev Yom Kippur, before Kol Nidrei, 5712.

### With the help of Hashem. The Rebbe’s Blessing to the Students Erev Yom Kippur, before Kol Nidrei, 5712.

*Unedited*

Since you are studying in the Rebbe’s yeshivah, you are the Rebbe’s *children* ("zait ir dem Rebbe'ns kinder")... and therefore, on Erev Yom Kippur, it is necessary to bless you with the "Blessing of the Children":

"And Hashem spoke to Moshe, saying: Speak to Aharon and to his sons, saying: This is how you shall bless the Children of Yisrael, saying to them: May Hashem bless you and keep you. May Hashem make His face shine upon you and be gracious to you. May Hashem lift His face to you and grant you peace. And they shall place My name upon the Children of Yisrael, and I will bless them".

May it be the will of Hashem that you have success in your study of Torah with yiras shamayim, and in fulfilling the Rebbe’s intent ("ir zolt oisfirn dem Rebbe'ns kavana").

May you be sealed and inscribed for a good year.

## With the help of Heaven. Motzoei Yom Kippur, 5712.

### With the help of Heaven. Motzoei Yom Kippur, 5712.

Unedited.
The Rebbe emerged from his holy room and stated that he did not intend to hold a farbrengen at this time, and that he would—with the help of Hashem—hold a farbrengen during Simchas Beis Hasho'eivah.
[One of those present remarked that the crowd wanted the Rebbe to hold a farbrengen, to which the Rebbe replied: "Not everything that is requested must be granted"...]
(And he added:) Farbreng among yourselves, and study the sichos of the Rebbe Rayatz from Motzoei Yom Kippur that are already available.
(And he concluded:) "A gutn yom-tov", "a gutn farbrengen".
[The Rebbe sent (via the secretary, Rabbi Chaim Mordechai Aizik Hodakov) "lekach" as a contribution to the farbrengen.]

## With the help of Hashem. Shabbos Parshas Haazinu, 13 Tishrei, 5712.

[Following Mincha, the Rebbe told several stories about the Baal HaHillula, Admur Maharash, of blessed memory:]

1. Before Rosh Hashanah of the year 5643 (the year of his passing), Admur Maharash said: "They will need to call a professor, to inject an injection, and to perform surgery." And so it happened. At the time the Maharash said these words, they did not grasp his intent, but later, at the time of his passing, the words were understood.

I heard this story from the grandmother (Rabbanit Sterna Sarah, mother of the Rebbe Rayatz) after forty years (!) had already passed since the passing, and yet, she told it in a way that *fear* was evident in her words!

2. Admur Maharash would *inspire awe* in everyone. The wonder of it was that a *smile* was always etched upon his holy face ("he was always with a smile"). Even though he was a man of great suffering [the Rebbe Rayatz said that it is difficult to imagine how great a sufferer he was...], nevertheless, a smile was always etched upon his face. Even during the lifetime of his father, Admur Tzemach Tzedek, the Maharash was less tense ("angezogen") than his other brothers. Despite this, he would *inspire awe* in all, even in children—a matter that occurred without any effort on his part, for naturally, a smile was etched upon his face; it was *spontaneous*.

Admur Maharash would also inspire awe in the non-Jews. It happened once that he was traveling by carriage to a certain city, and the elders of the city came out to greet him with bread and salt. When the carriage arrived and his holy face was seen, they all fled out of great fear!

At that time, Admur Maharash said a maamar of Chassidus on the verse "You shall be blessed above all peoples".

In this context, the Rebbe Rayatz once said (though he did not want the words to be publicized), that it was his settled opinion ("by him it settles") that the difference between Admur Maharash (his grandfather) and Admur (Rashab) (his father) is like the difference between *ratzon* (will) and *taanug* (pleasure):

Both are *makkif* (encompassing) powers, but *ratzon* effects a breaking ("ratzon breaks"), whereas *taanug* effects an drawing down and drawing close ("taanug draws near").

And in this instance: Admur Maharash is like *ratzon*, and therefore he inspired awe, whereas Admur (Rashab) is like *taanug*.

3. A contractor once came to Admur Tzemach Tzedek to ask for a blessing. The Tzemach Tzedek blessed him, and he indeed succeeded greatly. The contractor came to Admur Tzemach Tzedek and brought him a carriage as a gift. The Tzemach Tzedek said to him: "I have no need for this; give it to my son, the Maharash".

With Admur Tzemach Tzedek, conduct in material matters was not in a manner of expansion, to the extent that the chairs were not painted. Whereas with Admur Maharash—even during the lifetime of Admur Tzemach Tzedek—the conduct was the opposite, to the point that there were even expensive curtains on the windows of his house.

4. Admur Maharash would say Chassidus even during the lifetime of his father, the Tzemach Tzedek. There was also a time (before that) when he would say Chassidus in a way that no one knew about it. His custom was to lock the door, arrange chairs, and he would point and say: "This is the Radatz, and this is the Rashbatz," and so on with other Chassidim, and he would say Chassidus "before them".

Later, during his leadership, the order for saying Chassidus before the Chassidim was that after everyone entered, the doors were locked and it was impossible to leave. If someone would doze off in the middle of the saying of Chassidus, they would place "tzemeritze" before him—a powder with a very sharp scent, until he would begin to sneeze... (special people were appointed for this task!). Thus, everyone knew that once you entered, you could not leave, and whoever dozed off immediately received a "pask"...

5. I heard from Chassidim that during the week of mourning for the passing of Admur Maharash, Admur (Rashab) and R. Y.M. Bezpalov would walk back and forth in the hall of the Beis Medrash ("arumgein ibern zal") in their socks only (because of the mourning), and speak in Chassidus.

I doubt the veracity of the story, because the mourning was only for a few hours (since the passing was on 13 Tishrei toward evening, and the funeral was on the eve of the Yom Tov, and with the onset of the holiday the mourning ended). It is therefore difficult to say that in those few hours they managed to snatch ("haben zei shoin areingechapt")—while walking in their socks—to speak in Chassidus! Especially considering the depth of the *hiskashrus* of Admur (Rashab) to his father.

However, one should not raise difficulties regarding Chassidim ("oif Chassidim is kein kashya nit"), and even if the event did not occur, "a person is not suspected of a matter unless...".

6. In this context, they tell of the strength of Rabbanit Devorah Leah, daughter of Admur Maharash, that when she learned of her father's passing, she turned and faced the wall, and remained in that position for three days (!) and knew nothing of what was happening around her; her voice was not heard, etc.

7. The Rebbe Rayatz told that Admur Maharash had vast knowledge in the science of medicine, and he would write "retseptn" (prescriptions) for medicines himself and send them to the pharmacy. In "that place" he had a shelf with books in Latin, and when he was free, he would study them, and thus he learned the science of medicine.

It is worth noting that we find a parallel regarding *Shmuel* (the name by which Admur Maharash was also called)—who was "the physician of the Rebbe," because he was knowledgeable in the science of medicine, and he testified about himself that he did not engage in these matters "except at a time when I was free from Torah; when? When I would enter the lavatory".

8. Admur Maharash was ill even during the lifetime of his father, the Tzemach Tzedek, but he did not inform his father of this. When the Tzemach Tzedek learned of the matter, he said that had he known in time, he could have acted to extend his years. He would have acted so that he would live at least 52 years, like the prophet Shmuel.

9. When Admur Maharash visited the professor for the last time, the latter said to him: "Idtzi, idtzi" (Go, go), you can travel to your home in Lubavitch.

Admur Maharash responded and said: From this world to the World to Come—there is also "Idtzi, idtzi" (Go, go)...

10. At the time of the passing, Admur Maharash sat on his chair (for in the days preceding his passing, he would sit on his chair the entire time, even while sleeping).

A short time (a few minutes) before the passing, he took his watch (or asked that they bring him a watch), and turned the hands of the watch so that they would point to a certain time later on, and he took a piece of paper and inserted it (using a quill) inside the watch so that it would stop moving. And at exactly that time—to which he had set the watch—he passed away!...

11. Admur Maharash would not toil in his learning, because he had no need for it; he knew everything without toil. Once, the Tzemach Tzedek spoke with him about the virtue of toil in Torah, and from then on he began to labor and toil in Torah, to the extent that stains formed on his forehead from the magnitude of the toil. After some time, the Tzemach Tzedek retracted ("er hot tzurik gezoygen"), and gave him a new order for his learning.

## Sicha of the Second Day of Sukkos, 5712

[The Rebbe washed his hands for the meal. Afterward, he instructed that the entire gathering should wash their hands for the meal.]

1. I wish to propose that we "seize the moment" (*areinkhapn*) now to rejoice in the joy of the Yom Tov. The joy following Havdalah is the "Simchas Beis HaShoeivah," which "the common people and just anyone who wished were not permitted to perform; only the great sages of Israel... and the Chassidim, the elders, and the men of deed" (whereas "all the people—men and women—would come only to see and hear"). This is in contrast to the joy of now—the joy of Yom Tov—where "a person is obligated to be... happy and of good heart, he, his children, his wife, his grandchildren, and all who are dependent upon him, as it is written, 'And you shall rejoice in your festival,' etc.... each according to what is appropriate for him; for example, for the little ones he gives roasted grains, etc., and for the women he buys nice clothing and jewelry, etc.". In other words, the joy of Yom Tov is not only something that pertains to everyone, but more than that—*everyone is obligated in it*. And since the Torah demands this joy from each and every person, surely the necessary strengths to achieve it are granted to each and every person.

2. Regarding the mitzvah of Sukkah, it is said : "You shall dwell in Sukkos for seven days, etc., for I made the Children of Israel dwell in Sukkos when I brought them out of the land of Egypt." That is to say, Hashem commands the Children of Israel to *dwell* in Sukkos—"dwell as you would live" —for seven days; "all seven days a person makes his Sukkah his permanent home". He continues to explain the reason for the command—"*for* (which implies providing a reason) I made the Children of Israel dwell in Sukkos when I brought them out of the land of Egypt." This means that this mitzvah is a "*remembrance of the Exodus from Egypt*," when Hashem made the Children of Israel dwell in Sukkos—according to both interpretations of this: the Clouds of Glory or actual booths. It is explained in the Tur that "even though we left Egypt in the month of *Nissan*, He did not command us to build a Sukkah at that time, because it is the summer days, and it is the way of every person to build a booth for shade, and our act would not be recognizable as being in accordance with the command of the Creator, blessed be He. Therefore, He commanded us to do it in the *seventh* month (Tishrei), which is the rainy season, when it is the way of every person to leave their booth and sit in their house, and we leave the house to sit in the Sukkah; by this, it will be visible to all that the command of the King is upon us to perform it."

One must explain the moral lesson to be learned from the mitzvah of dwelling in the Sukkah (just as one must learn a moral lesson from every mitzvah), including its being fixed specifically in the rainy season, as follows.

3. By way of introduction: Our holy Torah is called "Toras Chaim" (the Torah of life), because its subject and content encompass and permeate the entire life of a person, from the moment of birth until after one hundred and twenty years. That is to say, the matter of Torah and mitzvos is not such that one is under an obligation to perform certain actions at certain times and afterward becomes free to behave as he pleases. Rather, it is in a manner that permeates and encompasses *his entire life*, so that *every single matter he engages in* must be according to the command and instruction of the Torah.

And more than this—as is brought in Chassidus, the ultimate goal of avodah is that even the *sleep* of a Jew (when he is not performing any action) must be according to Torah, such that even during sleep it should be recognizable that he is a Jew. And since this is demanded of him, it is surely within his power to achieve this for himself—because even during sleep, since the *kista d'chiyuta* (spark of vitality) remains in him, he is the master of himself. Proof of this is from the law in the revealed Torah that "a person is always liable, etc., whether awake or asleep" ; meaning, he is liable even for damage caused during sleep, because even then he is the master of himself.

This matter (that even during sleep it is recognizable that he is a Jew) is achieved by the fact that *before* sleep he *prepares and lies down* to sleep ("*er leigt zich shlofn*") as a Jew—being permeated with the knowledge and recognition that even during sleep "Hashem stands over him... and examines the kidneys and the heart", and even then he is the servant of the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He. This preparation (before sleep) acts upon the sleep, so that the sleep itself is the sleep of a servant.

One can bring proof that the preparation before sleep acts upon the sleep: we see tangibly that when a person lies down to sleep with the resolve to wake up at a certain time, he wakes from his sleep at the time he decided to wake. That is to say, even though the decision was before sleep, and afterward he is asleep, nevertheless, since he decided with a complete resolve before sleep, the decision acts even during sleep. And so it is in our case—that when he *lies down* to sleep as is proper (out of the knowledge and recognition that "Hashem stands over him"), this causes even the *sleep itself* to be as is proper, where not only will no undesirable matters occur to him during sleep, G-d forbid, but on the contrary, his soul will ascend on high to draw life for itself, to receive an addition of strength and vitality, etc.

4. Furthermore: This matter, that the Torah is "Toras Chaim" which permeates and encompasses all of a person's life, is in full force at all times and in all situations, for the Torah is eternal. A Jew might argue: Such conduct—that all of a person's life should be permeated with Torah—was possible *in the time of the Beis HaMikdash*, in a state and situation of light and revelation ("*ven s'iz geven lichtig*"), whereas *in the time of exile*, in a state and situation of darkness—how can one achieve such conduct?!

The answer to this—as mentioned—is that the Torah is eternal, and consequently, it is "Toras Chaim" not only in the time of the Beis HaMikdash, but also in the time of exile. And on the contrary: because of the intensification of darkness in the time of exile, one must add even more in matters of Torah in order to illuminate the darkness of the exile.

By way of introduction—this is the way of Torah: "It is known in the Gemara that most of the decrees, stringencies, and safeguards ('make a safeguard for My safeguard') were specifically in the time of the Second Beis HaMikdash," which was inferior to the First, and many of them were specifically after the destruction. And so, from generation to generation, more fences and safeguards are added to the Torah (in addition to the innovations in Torah, "everything that a veteran student will eventually innovate"). It is also worth noting that in every Rosh Hashanah, it was customary to accept upon oneself to add in matters of Torah and mitzvos, extra caution in negative mitzvos, beautification in positive mitzvos, or an addition in good conduct.

Seemingly, how is it possible to add new matters now? In the time of the Beis HaMikdash these matters did not exist, and specifically now they will add them?! The explanation for this is that this is precisely the reason: specifically because the darkness of the exile is growing ("*der choshech vert altz gresser un tiefer*"), one must add even more in matters of light and holiness to illuminate the darkness. From this, it is also understood that specifically in the time of exile, in a state and situation of darkness, there must be extra effort (not to suffice with his avodah with himself, but) to go out and illuminate the street as well.

5. All of this is emphasized in the content of the mitzvah of Sukkah: First and foremost, regarding the manner of fulfilling the mitzvah of Sukkah —that all of a person's matters, his eating and drinking, etc., and even his sleep, are done in the Sukkah, and in them and through them he fulfills the mitzvah of Sukkah. This emphasizes that all of a person's matters are permeated with the mitzvos of the Torah, as mentioned, that the Torah is "Toras Chaim."

Furthermore, and essentially, regarding the fixing of the time for the mitzvah of Sukkah specifically in the month of Tishrei, and not in the month of Nissan (in which they left Egypt): Just as the departure to the Sukkah in its literal sense is recognized and considered a *mitzvah* not in the month of Nissan, the summer days, when the sun shines in its strength, and then the departure to the Sukkah is the way of the world for the sake of a person's comfort—but only when it is done in the days of Tishrei, the winter days, after the strength of the sun has weakened, and outside cold winds blow and rains fall (which is why the way of the world for the sake of a person's comfort is to enter the houses), so too is it in spiritual avodah:

In the month of Nissan, the time of the Exodus from Egypt, the summer days, when the light of the sun, the "Sun of Hashem", shines in its strength, and from day to day there is an addition in the revelation of the "Sun of Hashem"—then, when a Jew *leaves his house* (to the Sukkah, the content of which departure is) *to illuminate the outside*—there is no mitzvah in this, for it is a good and comfortable thing ("*s'iz pshat gut*"). Specifically in the month of Tishrei, after the strength of the sun has weakened, when the revelation of the "Sun of Hashem" does not shine in its strength, and to the point that it does not shine at all, so that outside there is *darkness*, and furthermore, cold winds blow, etc.—then there is the obligation (of the mitzvah of Sukkah, the content of which is) that a Jew leave the house *to illuminate the street*!

And when one conducts oneself in the aforementioned manner—that even though one is in a time and state and situation of darkness and cold, nevertheless, one leaves the house (to the Sukkah) to illuminate the street—then one merits the fulfillment of the prophecy, "All the native-born in Israel shall dwell in Sukkos", "the native-born (*ha'ezrach*) is a term for the future, that which I am destined to cause to shine (*hazriach*)... in the time to come".

6. Based on the above, one must explain the content of the *Ushpizin* (guests) on the festival of Sukkos: It is stated in the Zohar that on the festival of Sukkos, seven *Ushpizin* come to the Sukkah—Avraham, Yitzchak, Yaakov, Moshe, Aharon, Yosef, and David. Seemingly, it is not understood: what is the reason for the coming of the *Ushpizin* to the Sukkah specifically on the festival of Sukkos—a matter we do not find in other mitzvos, and in other festivals, neither on the festival of Pesach nor on the festival of Shavuos?!

The explanation for this: The content of the mitzvah of Sukkah in spiritual avodah is—as mentioned—that one should not be impressed by the darkness and cold in the street; on the contrary, one must leave the house to the Sukkah in order to illuminate the street. It is understood that when one demands of a Jew to go out to a dark and cold street to illuminate it, surely one does not leave him alone... rather, one gives him the necessary strengths for this. This, therefore, is the content of the coming of the *Ushpizin* on the festival of Sukkos—*the giving of strength* for the avodah of the rainy days, that even after the strength of the sun has weakened, in a state and situation of darkness and cold, they will be able to illuminate the street. This matter is within the power of the *Ushpizin*, beginning *with Avraham Avinu*, who sacrificed his soul and opened the channel of *mesiras nefesh* (self-sacrifice) for all the Children of Israel (and similarly regarding the other *Ushpizin*).

7. Besides the *Ushpizin* mentioned in the Zohar, in recent generations, more *Ushpizin* have been added—as the words of the Rebbe Rayatz that "our *Ushpizin* ('*undzere ushpizin*') are: the Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid of Mezeritch, the Alter Rebbe, the Mitteler Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, the Rebbe Maharash, and the Rebbe Rashab." He (the Rebbe Rayatz) added that one should endeavor to mention these *Ushpizin* during the days of the festival of Sukkos.

Regarding the aforementioned *Ushpizin*, they asked me: And what about the Rebbe Rayatz? The answer to this: The Rebbe Rayatz is the *eighth* Nasi, and therefore, his connection is (not to the seven days of Sukkos in which the seven *Ushpizin* come, but) to *Shemini Atzeres*. (It is worth noting what is written in the Zohar that Shemini Atzeres corresponds to *Yosef*—the first name of the Rebbe Rayatz). It is called "Atzeres" because in it the *internalization* occurs of all the illuminations and lights that are revealed and shine in the festivals of the month of Tishrei, and especially on the festival of Sukkos. And regarding this it is written, "On the eighth day, there shall be an Atzeres for *you*, etc., and you shall offer, etc., one bull, one ram," corresponding to the "unique nation", "as it is said, 'They shall be *for you alone*, and no strangers with you'". This is a matter more exalted than the seven days of Sukkos, in which they offered seventy bulls corresponding to the seventy nations of the world. Whereas on Shemini Atzeres they offer "one bull, one ram," corresponding to the unique nation, as it is stated in the Midrash : "A parable of a king who made a feast for seven days and invited all the people of the country... once the seven days of the feast passed, he said to his beloved, 'We have already fulfilled our obligation to all the people of the country; let us celebrate, *I and you*, with what you find... with one bull and one ram.'"

In any case, for the time being, we have not reached Shemini Atzeres, but we are still standing in the days of Sukkos, in which the seven *Ushpizin* come, both the *Ushpizin* in the Zohar and the *Ushpizin* of the Torah of Chassidus, as mentioned above. The reason for the addition in the matter of the *Ushpizin* in recent generations is due to the intensification of the darkness: It was explained above (section 4) that as the darkness grows and intensifies, one must add more in light and holiness. For this reason, the general Torah of Chassidus and the Torah of Chabad Chassidus were revealed specifically in recent generations—because, due to the intensification of the darkness, there is a need for an extra addition in light and holiness. From this, it is also understood regarding the matter of the *Ushpizin*—the content of which is the giving of strength to go out and illuminate the street in the rainy days, in a state of darkness and cold (as mentioned in section 6)—that due to the *intensification of the darkness*, the giving of strength through the *Ushpizin* in the Zohar, Avraham, etc., is not sufficient, but there is a need for an *addition of strength* through additional *Ushpizin*: the Nesi'im of the general Torah of Chassidus and the Nesi'im of the Torah of Chabad Chassidus. With this strength, one goes out to illuminate the darkness outside, and ultimately one reaches the state and situation of "an Atzeres for you," "they shall be for you alone, and no strangers with you."

8. One must add that since the general content of the *Ushpizin* is *assistance and the giving of strength from above* for the general avodah in the rainy days, this is in a manner that they give from above *most exalted* strengths, which are not according to any proportion at all, and they give them *all at once* ("*m'git op altz mitamol*"). [Based on this, one must explain the difference between Sukkos and Chanukah, that the order of offering the festival bulls (in Sukkos) is in a manner of "decreasing," whereas the order of lighting the Chanukah candles is in a manner of "increasing" —because the avodah of Chanukah (to illuminate the darkness, "at the entrance of his house from the outside") is *from below to above*, and therefore the order of avodah is from the easy to the difficult, "increasing." Whereas Sukkos, when the *giving of strength from above* is drawn down (as a *preface* to the avodah from below to above to illuminate the darkness), this is in a manner that they give from the outset the most exalted strengths, and afterward there is no need for such exalted strengths, and therefore it is in a manner of decreasing].

This matter is emphasized in the verse that Avraham, the first *Ushpiza*, says—as it is stated in the Zohar that each of the seven *Ushpizin* says a verse in the Torah in which he blesses the Jew sitting in the Sukkah—"*Then you shall delight in Hashem*", "in *Hashem*" specifically, which means *above the Name Havayah*, which is the most exalted level, not according to any proportion at all (as follows), and this exalted level is revealed and shines immediately at the beginning of the festival of Sukkos.

9. Explanation of the matter: The Name Havayah is above the Name Elokim, because the Name Elokim (from the word *koach*—strength) indicates the level of G-dliness that pertains to the creation of the world, as it is written, "In the beginning, Elokim created," "the Name Elokim is said 32 times in the account of Creation". Whereas the Name Havayah, despite it also being from the word *mehaveh* (bringing into being), the bringing into being from the Name Havayah is in a manner of "was, is, and will be" as one, meaning, above the limitations of time, and consequently also above the limitations of place, above nature. Whereas the bringing into being from the Name Elokim is according to nature, "Elokim" in *gematria* is "HaTeva" (nature).

More specifically—there are three modes in the reality of the world: (a) "Olam" (world) from the word *he'elem* (concealment) —as it conceals and hides G-dliness, so that the G-dly vitality in the world is not seen; (b) above this—the world as it is from the perspective of being brought into being by the Name Elokim, in *gematria* "HaTeva"—where *G-dly vitality* is seen and felt in the world [for just as "Elokim" in *gematria* is "HaTeva," so too conversely, "HaTeva" in *gematria* is "Elokim," meaning, in nature itself G-dliness is seen and felt], but only the level of G-dliness *that is clothed in nature* ; (c) and above this—the world as it is from the perspective of being brought into being by the Name Havayah, "was, is, and will be" as one, meaning, that the level of G-dliness *that is above nature* shines in the world.

One must add that what is being discussed regarding the most exalted level as the world is from the perspective of the Name Havayah—refers not only to this world, but also includes the delight of the *World to Come* (of which they said, "You shall see your world in your lifetime"), for our Sages said, "With the letter *Hei* this world was created, with the letter *Yud* the World to Come was created," meaning, this world is the letter *Hei* of the Name Havayah, and the World to Come is the letter *Yud of the Name Havayah*.

And after all the aforementioned elevations, there is a more exalted level—"Then you shall delight *in Hashem*," *above* the Name Havayah, which level is above even the delight of the World to Come that is drawn from the *Yud* of the Name Havayah. For the delight of the World to Come, despite being above this world, nevertheless has a connection to this world, as is emphasized by the fact that it is called "the World to Come" ("not because it does not exist now... for it exists and stands," but) "because those lives come to a person *after the life of this world*", meaning, there is a value and connection between them. Whereas the level of "Then you shall delight *in Hashem*" has no connection to this world at all.

10. And more deeply—"Then you shall delight in Hashem," above the Name Havayah (including even the *Yud* of the Name Havayah) even as it is before the *Tzimtzum* (contraction). By way of introduction : Even though before the *Tzimtzum* there is no division of details and levels, nevertheless, even before the *Tzimtzum* there is the matter of the Name Havayah, such a matter that from its perspective the Name Havayah after the *Tzimtzum* is made (even if not in a manner that it becomes the *root* for the Name Havayah after the *Tzimtzum*).

The explanation for this is by way of a parable of a teacher and a student, an influencer and a recipient, who are not in any proportion to each other at all. Even though the intellect that pertains to the student does not occupy any place at all relative to the intellect of the teacher, nevertheless, when the teacher thinks about the influence to the student, then the intellect that pertains to the student is felt by him (including the order of influence that is hinted at in the four letters of the Name Havayah). However, this is as the intellect that is for the student *exists within the teacher* (the influencer), where it does not pertain to the student (the recipient) at all, but from this, the revelation of the intellect that pertains to the student will be drawn down afterward.

The analogy in the subject—that even before the *Tzimtzum* there is the light that is in proportion to and *for* the worlds, which is the matter of the Name Havayah, which after all the elevations in it is only a *Name* that is for the *sake of the other* (the worlds). However, this is as it is before the *Tzimtzum*, where it is not in any proportion at all to the worlds, but from this, the revelation will be drawn down afterward into the worlds.

11. Explanation of the matter in more detail: The order of influence from teacher to student who are not in any proportion to each other at all—even though within the teacher there is also the intellect that is for the student, nevertheless, since it is only the externality of the intellect, and is not in any proportion at all to the intellect of the teacher himself, the teacher must contract his intellect to the point of a contraction in the manner of total removal, and only then can he *find within himself*—when he wishes—the externality of the intellect that pertains to the student.

Furthermore: Even after the externality of the intellect that pertains to the student is felt by the teacher (by his removing his intellect totally)—it is also recognizable and felt in the externality of the intellect (the connection to) the *teacher* ("*es hert zich on rav*"), like in the intellect that pertains to himself. Therefore, we see that even in the actual influence of the intellect to the student, there are differences (in the influenced intellect) from the essence of the teacher, whether he is a small scholar, a great scholar, or a scholar wondrous in his wisdom—even though the influence of the intellect comes after the removal of the influencer's intellect totally—because even in the externality of the intellect, the teacher is recognizable and felt. Therefore, there must be the action of *Tzimtzum* also *in the externality of the intellect itself* (in addition to the fact that the revelation of the externality of the intellect is through the *Tzimtzum*)—*that it should change* from how it is with the teacher to be in a manner that pertains to the student.

And more than that, even after the *Tzimtzum*, the influence must be in an orderly manner—hinted at in the four letters of the Name Havayah: Even after the externality of the intellect is revealed in a manner that pertains to the student (through the *Tzimtzum*), at the beginning of the revelation it is only in a manner of a *point* alone, like the letter *Yud* of the Name Havayah, which is in the form of a point alone, the point of the *reshimu* (impression), in which is revealed (only) the intent of the *Tzimtzum*, the intent and will of the influencer to reveal. Although in this point exists all the intellect that pertains to and is influenced to the recipient, it is in a manner of a point alone, and from a point alone the influence cannot be to the student.

Afterward, the point comes in a manner of expansion *in length and width*—like the letter *Hei* of the Name Havayah, which has length and width. And even after the point of intellect comes in expansion in length and width, since the closeness to the influencer is still felt ("*s'iz doch ersht nachn tzimtzum*"), the influencer must distance the intellect from himself—as hinted at in the letter *Vav* of the Name Havayah, which indicates the drawing down from above to below, in distance from the influencer, where there (below, in distance from the influencer) the influence of the influencer comes (which is hinted at in the point, *Yud*, which is at the head of the *Vav*).

However, all this is only that the intellect has distanced itself from the influencer, and afterward the intellect must come into settlement and absorption in the recipient—like the *final Hei* of the Name Havayah, which is drawn into the expanse of the recipient. And since after the *Tzimtzum* the influence of the teacher to the student must be in the aforementioned manner and order (hinted at in the four letters of the Name Havayah), it must be that the manner and order of the influence (in addition to the influenced intellect) is already fixed within him ("*s'iz shoin oisgeshtelt bei im*") even *before* the influence to the recipient—immediately when he thinks about the recipient, even *before he contracts* his intellect in order to reveal within himself the externality of the intellect that pertains to the recipient. And although at this level it is not in any proportion at all to the recipient, nevertheless, it is not as it is for himself, but as he thinks about a recipient, and therefore it is effective after a time when he comes to the actual influence.

12. From this, it is also understood in the analogy—that even before the *Tzimtzum* there is the (four letters of) the Name Havayah: Since the light that pertains to and is *for* the worlds is not in any proportion at all relative to His Essence, blessed be He, there must be a *Tzimtzum* in the way of total removal, which is the matter of the first *Tzimtzum*, through which the externality of the light that pertains to the worlds was revealed. And even afterward, the influence for the sake of the creation of the worlds comes in a manner of contraction and expansion, etc., which is the matter of the four letters of the Name Havayah.

However, even before the *Tzimtzum* there is the light that pertains to and is *for* the worlds, which, although it is not yet a source for the worlds—for for the sake of the creation of the worlds, a *Tzimtzum* in the way of total removal is specifically necessary—nevertheless, it already has some *connection to the worlds*—which is the matter of the Name, the Name Havayah, which even while being above the form of the influence of the four letters, is a *Name* whose content is *for the sake of the other* (the worlds). And above this—His Essence, blessed be He, as He is from His own perspective, which is not in any proportion at all to the light that pertains to and is *for* the worlds even as it is before the *Tzimtzum* (like the intellect of the teacher as it is for itself, before he thinks about the recipient).

13. Based on this, one must explain the greatness of the festival of Sukkos, in which the matter of "Then you shall delight *in Hashem*" (the verse that the first *Ushpiza* says) is revealed—above the Name Havayah, above even the Name Havayah as it is before the *Tzimtzum*: It is known that the influences of Rosh Hashanah are revealed on the festival of Sukkos, as it is written, "Blow the shofar in the month, at the covering for the day of our festival," that the influences of Rosh Hashanah, which at that time are still covered ("*b'keseh*"), are revealed on the festival of Sukkos ("for the day of our festival").

Now, the content of Rosh Hashanah is (as it is written in the psalm said before the shofar blowing) "He will choose for us our inheritance", the matter of choice, which is from the perspective of the *Essence* specifically. And this matter is revealed on the festival of Sukkos—when essential revelations shine, the revelation of the choice that is from the perspective of the Essence, above even the Name Havayah as it is before the *Tzimtzum* ("Then you shall delight *in Hashem*").

One must add that the revelation of "Then you shall delight in Hashem" (above the Name Havayah) is drawn down and revealed also in the Name Havayah—as hinted at in the taking of the Four Species, which correspond to the four letters of the Name Havayah (and as the Taz brings from the Beis Yosef in the name of the Rekanati, that he saw in a dream someone "writing the Name with *Yud Hei*, and was distancing the final *Hei* from the three letters," because "he was not shaking only the lulav and its species without the esrog... for all the Four Species hint at Him, blessed be He, etc.").

14. However, there are those who ask: What is the effect of all the revelations, up to the most exalted revelation of "Then you shall delight in Hashem"—at the same time that they do not feel these revelations, and do not pertain to them, and how is it possible that through their avodah they will draw down such exalted revelations ?!

The answer to this—by way of introduction: The inquiry is known —in the revealed Torah—regarding things that are forbidden due to a decree: is the entire force of the prohibition only because of the decree alone, and consequently, in a place where the decree does not pertain, the prohibition is nullified? Or, after the prohibition is established (even because of a decree alone), one no longer considers the reason for the prohibition, but it becomes an essential prohibition?

One can bring proof that even a prohibition because of a decree becomes an essential prohibition—from the laws of Sukkah: One may not roof with boards that have four *tefachim* (which most house ceilings are made of), because of the "decree of the ceiling," for "if you permit them, one might come to say, 'What is the difference to me if I roof with these or if I sit under the beams of my house? It too is roofed with boards,' and that is certainly invalid, for the Torah said 'Sukkah' and not the house of all the days of the year".

And in the continuation of the passage : "If he turned them on their sides (which is less than three *tefachim*), what is the law?"—in which the "decree of the ceiling" does not pertain, for "in such a manner people do not make a ceiling"—"*it is invalid*, they are made like metal spits," "for since there is a *name of invalidity upon them*, they are made like metal spits which are invalid for roofing in any manner that he turns them." From this it is proven that even a thing that was forbidden because of a decree (a board that has four *tefachim* which is forbidden because of the decree of the ceiling) becomes an essential prohibition, without considering the

## Sicha of the Night Following the First Day of Chol Hamoed Sukkos, Simchas Beis Hashoevah 5712

**Unedited**

**1.** Regarding Simchas Beis Hashoevah, the Gemara states: "From where is this derived (that we sound the *tekios* and *teruos* during the water-drawing for the libation)? ... As the verse says: 'And you shall draw water with joy' (Yeshayahu 12:3)." This means that the verse "And you shall draw water" refers to the drawing of water for the libation upon the Altar, and therefore it says, "And you shall draw water *with joy*," implying that the drawing of the water must be done with joy. Thus, we find that the primary joy was (not at the time of the water libation upon the Altar, but) specifically at the time of the *drawing of the water*.

However, the proof from the verse "And you shall draw water with joy" only establishes the requirement for *joy* during the water-drawing. Yet, in the Mishnah and Gemara it is stated (not merely that there must be joy, but something even greater): "Whoever has not seen the joy of the Beis Hashoevah has never seen joy in his life." This means that the water-drawing was performed with *great joy*, even more than the joy of the festival itself—and this is difficult to understand:

Regarding the joy of the festival, there is an explicit verse in the Torah regarding the Yom Tov: "And you shall rejoice in your festival" (Devarim 16:14). This is not the case with "And you shall draw water with joy," which is stated as a general verse. However, since we find no obligation for water-drawing other than for the purpose of the water libation upon the Altar, we learn this verse as referring to the water-drawing for the libation.

And yet, the joy of the water-drawing (which must be derived from the verse "And you shall draw water with joy") is greater than the joy of the festival (which is explicitly stated in the text).

The question therefore arises: From where is this derived? What is the proof for this?

**2.** This can be explained by first noting a parallel to what we find regarding the festival of Pesach.

As is known, the month of Tishrei and the month of Nisan are equivalent: Tishrei is the "Rosh Hashanah" and Nisan is the "head of the months," and also in the festivals that fall within them (Sukkos and Pesach), there are several matters that are comparable to one another.
