[Similar to what is explained in the discourses of *Chassidus* regarding the matter of "He stumbled in the iniquity of my strength," that the iniquities touch ("*rirn on*") even the essence of the soul—even though the essence of the soul is certainly not guilty of it.]

But what then? He has a complaint: It is true that as the "head," all the community’s affairs touch him, but why must he suffer for matters that are not his fault?!—The meaning of this (that all the community’s affairs touch him) is not that he will receive punishment, *chas v'shalom* (for it is simple that one cannot be punished for something that is not his fault), but rather, that he does not receive the elevated matters he could have received had the leadership of the community been as it should be. This is similar to what we find with Moshe Rabbeinu, that after the sin of the Golden Calf (which was certainly not his fault), he was told, "Go, descend,"—"Descend from your greatness; did I give you greatness for any reason other than for the sake of Yisroel?"

However, even though there is no punishment here, but rather only a lack of receiving reward, nevertheless, according to what is explained in *Chassidus* regarding the interpretation of the Mishnah's statement, "The reward of a *mitzvah* is the *mitzvah* [itself]," that the true reward is (the *mitzvah* itself, through which one achieves) *tzavta* (a connection) and union with the Essence and Being of the *Ein Sof*, may He be blessed—than which there is no greater reward—and according to the magnitude of the reward is the magnitude of the loss and damage in the absence of receiving that reward—it is understood that the fact that he does not receive the reward he could have received had the community’s leadership been as it should be, constitutes a great loss and damage!

**6.** And just as these things are said regarding the Rabbi, so too is it regarding the *shochet*:
The Rebbe Rayatz said that the Rabbi is the "head" of the community, and the *shochet* is the "*heart*" of the community.
A "*shochet*"—the Rebbe Rayatz said—is not a "slaughterer," a man who holds a knife in his hand and kills animals... A "*shochet*" is the "*heart*" of the community, and he must be the spirit of life of the community, organizing study sessions for Torah and the like. In addition to this, he is also engaged in the craft of *shechitah*, but that is not his primary *avodah*.

And it must be added regarding the craft of *shechitah* itself, that "it requires checking the flesh and the knife," "he checked it on the tip of his tongue"—which is to say, its meaning in *avodah* is that the *shochet* must check himself so that he does not have "claws" that prick... and he must also check his speech, the content of his words, and their style, so that they should be as they ought to be. Otherwise, he is nothing but a "slaughterer," a man with a knife who kills animals, and then the animal complains against him: "Why are you taking my life? In what way are you better than me?!"...

*

**7.** [The Rebbe instructed the yeshiva students to say "L’chaim," and then said:]

Following what was discussed earlier regarding the three levels in Torah—the level of Torah as it comes by inheritance, the level of Torah as it comes through toil, and the level of Torah as it is given as a gift—it must be added and explained in more detail.

The first level (from bottom to top), the lowest in Torah, is as it comes *by inheritance*:
Inheritance is not dependent on the son’s status or situation, his traits, merits, etc., but rather on the very fact of his being a son, to the extent that even while he is a fetus in his mother’s womb, he is an heir.

Its meaning in Torah is the level of Torah that belongs to every single Yisroel, regardless of his status or situation, just as in inheritance one does not take into account the status or situation of the heir—the level of Torah that belongs to *the fulfillment of the mitzvos*. This is the meaning of "Torah"—from the word *hora'ah* (instruction), to instruct the action that they shall do and those that they shall not do. This matter belongs to every single Yisroel, for even those who are not capable of grasping the Torah are obligated to know the action they shall do (the part of the Torah that belongs to the fulfillment of the *mitzvos*), and if they do not know, they must ask and clarify from one who knows—similar to a minor heir who needs a guardian.

This matter is hinted at in the teaching of our Sages, "*Torah* commanded to us by Moshe is an *inheritance* (*morasha*), Torah in *gematria* is 611; 'I am' and 'You shall have no other' we heard from the mouth of the Almighty" (meaning, as it is written, "Torah commanded to us by Moshe," and two from the mouth of the Almighty, that is 613)—in which it is hinted that the level of Torah that comes *by inheritance* ("*morasha*") is the level of Torah that belongs to *the fulfillment of the 613 mitzvos* (Torah in *gematria* is 611, excluding "I am" and "You shall have no other" which we heard from the mouth of the Almighty).

**8.** And it must be added in explanation of the connection of the level of Torah that belongs to the fulfillment of the *mitzvos* to the matter of inheritance:
By way of introduction—the innovation of the Giving of the Torah compared to before the Giving of the Torah (the *avodah* of the Patriarchs, who fulfilled the entire Torah before it was given) is regarding the fulfillment of the *mitzvos* *in physicality*. As our Sages said, "All the *mitzvos* that the Patriarchs did before You were *scents*," only *in spirituality*. That is to say, although the Patriarchs also fulfilled the *mitzvos* with physical objects, nevertheless, it was only that they fulfilled the *mitzvos* *by means of* physical objects, but the *action* that is accomplished by the fulfillment of the *mitzvos* (the drawing down of *Elokus*) was only *in spirituality*, in the world of *Atzilus*, etc., while in the physical object with which the *mitzvah* was performed, nothing was accomplished. For example: the converts that Avraham converted—nothing remained of them; and likewise, the sticks by means of which Yaakov drew down the influences of the *mitzvah* of *tefillin*—after the *avodah* with them was finished, no holiness remained in them at all. The innovation of the Giving of the Torah is that not only is the fulfillment of the *mitzvos* by means of physical objects, but the holiness is drawn down and fixed *in the physical objects* with which one fulfills the *mitzvos*, like in *tefillin*, which even at a time when one is not fulfilling the *mitzvah*, it is a *cheftza d’kedusha* (an object of holiness), and likewise with other articles of *mitzvos* and articles of holiness.

In the words of the *Midrash*: "A parable... to a king who decreed and said: 'The people of Rome shall not go down to Syria, and the people of Syria shall not go up to Rome.' Thus, when the Holy One, blessed be He, created the world, He decreed and said: 'The heavens are the heavens for Hashem, and the earth He gave to the sons of man.' When He sought to give the Torah, He nullified the first decree and said: 'The lower realms shall ascend to the upper realms, and the upper realms shall descend to the lower realms.'" That is to say, the innovation of the Giving of the Torah is *the connection of the upper and lower realms*, because through the fulfillment of the *mitzvos*, holiness is drawn down and fixed in the physical objects (lower realms) with which one fulfills the *mitzvos*, which become a vessel for *Elokus* (they shall ascend to the upper realms).

The point of the matter is that the fulfillment of the *mitzvos* is for the sake of the *avodah* of *birurim* (refining), to separate the good from the evil, by which one *repairs* the flaw that was made in the world by the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, which created a mixture of good and evil, and because of this, *death* was created in the world (so that there would be no existence for evil). Therefore, the level of Torah that belongs to the fulfillment of the *mitzvos*—whose purpose is to repair the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, because of which the matter of *death* was created—is called by the name *inheritance*.

**9.** Based on the above, that the level of Torah as it comes *by inheritance* is the level of Torah that belongs to the fulfillment of the *mitzvos* whose purpose is *to act in the world*—we must explain the reason that the prohibition for a non-Jew to study Torah was stated in connection to the level of inheritance in Torah:
It is stated in the *Gemara*: "A non-Jew who engages in Torah is liable for death, as it is said, 'Torah commanded to us by Moshe is an *inheritance* (*morasha*), to us an inheritance and not to them...' Some say *morasha* (inheritance), he is stealing it; some say *me'orasa* ('Do not read *morasha* but *me'orasa* [betrothed]'), his law is like a betrothed maiden, who is [punished] by stoning."
The matter is that in the level of Torah as it comes by inheritance ("*morasha*"), since its entire purpose is *to act in the world*, there is room to say that it also belongs to a non-Jew [especially since regarding the "seven *mitzvos* of theirs," they must be "engaged in the laws of those seven *mitzvos* to be proficient in them"]. Therefore, there is a need for a special study to exclude and limit a non-Jew from the study of Torah—"to us an inheritance and not to them, etc." (Whereas in a more elevated level in Torah, as it is above acting in the world (as follows), there is no need to exclude and limit a non-Jew).

**10.** And above this—the level of Torah as it comes specifically through *toil*:
The toil in Torah—in which not everyone is equal, like inheritance, but is a matter dependent on the *avodah* of man—its essence (not necessarily in the part of the Torah that belongs to the fulfillment of the *mitzvos*, but) is in the understanding and comprehension *of the wisdom of the Torah as it is in itself*, even if the matter does not touch upon actual practice in the fulfillment of the *mitzvos* (and in the words of the Alter Rebbe in *Tanya*, "even if this matter never was and never will be").

The explanation for this is that in addition to the purpose of the Torah to instruct the action that they shall do in the fulfillment of the *mitzvos*—which is the level of Torah as it belongs *to the world*, to instruct man how to behave in the world—there is also the purpose of the Torah as it is in itself ("a matter for itself, Torah as Torah")—that it is *the wisdom and will of the Holy One, blessed be He*.

This matter is not in the manner of inheritance that belongs to every single Yisroel regardless of his status or situation; rather, for this, there is a need for the *toil* of man specifically, and according to the measure of his toil in Torah, he understands and comprehends the wisdom of the Torah.

**11.** However, even the level of Torah as it comes in the level of toil, despite being the level of Torah as it is in itself (not only to act in the world), the wisdom and will of the Holy One, blessed be He, which are completely incomparable to the human intellect, nevertheless, since it comes through the toil of man in his intellect and understanding, it is at least within the bounds of the measurement of human intellect, albeit incomparably above it.
And regarding this it is said, "It is longer than the earth in measure, etc."—this matter is said about the level of Torah as it is in itself, as it is above the level of Torah whose purpose is to instruct on the fulfillment of the *mitzvos*, as the Alter Rebbe writes in the Laws of Torah Study that "*the laws* (the level of Torah whose purpose is to instruct on the fulfillment of the *mitzvos*)... have an end, a limit, and a number," and what is said, "It is longer than the earth in measure, etc.," refers to "*the Torah from its own side* (which) has no end or limit even to the literal interpretations hidden within it... and likewise there is no end or limit to the depth of the reasons for the laws and the *pilpul* in their reasons, etc."—that even though it is without limit, it is still *in the category of measure*, that it is measured with other matters, only that it is "*longer* than the earth in measure."

Whereas the most elevated level in Torah, which is above all measurement and limitation, and is not even in the category of measure—is the level of Torah as it is in His Essence, may He be blessed, "delights, etc., before Him," the delights of the King in His Essence.
And since this level is above all measurement and limitation, and is not even in the category of measure—it cannot come through the toil of man, and comes from above specifically by way of *gift*, as we say in the text of the blessing of the Torah: "*He gave* us His Torah... *the Giver* of the Torah."

**12.** And it must be added in the content of the matter of the blessing of the Torah:
It is stated in the *Gemara*: "What is the meaning of the verse, 'Who is the wise man who will understand this, and to whom the mouth of Hashem has spoken, that he may declare it: Why has the land perished?' This matter the Sages asked... the prophets (they asked the Sages and the prophets) and they did not explain it, until the Holy One, blessed be He, explained it Himself, as it is said: 'And Hashem said: Because they forsook My Torah which I set before them... that they did not bless the Torah first.'"

And the *Ran* explains that "the verse indicates precisely that it was because they did not bless the Torah first that the land perished. For if it were because they forsook My Torah as it literally implies, that they forsook the Torah and were not engaged in it, when the Sages and prophets were asked, why did they not explain it? Was it not a revealed matter and easy to explain? Rather, they were certainly engaged in Torah constantly, and therefore the Sages and prophets were puzzled as to why the land perished, until the Holy One, blessed be He, explained it Himself, for He knows the depths of the heart, that they were not blessing the Torah first—meaning, that the Torah was not so important in their eyes that it was worthy to bless over it, that they were not engaged in it for its own sake, and because of this, they were negligent in its blessing."

The explanation for this is that, seemingly, since "they were certainly engaged in Torah constantly," it must be that the Torah was important in their eyes, for otherwise, they would not be engaged and toiling in its study—that the importance of the Torah in their eyes was only from the side of the *intellect* within it, human intellect, even if it was a very deep intellect, but the Torah was not important in their eyes from the side of its true importance—as it is expressed in the blessing of the Torah: "He gave us His Torah"—*the Torah of the Holy One, blessed be He*, His wisdom and will, may He be blessed.

The study of Torah must therefore be from the recognition that the Torah is the Torah of the Holy One, blessed be He, and not only that, but *now* the Holy One, blessed be He, is giving the Torah, "the Giver of the Torah" in the present tense, which is why our Sages said, "Just as there it was with awe, fear, trembling, and shuddering, so too here it must be with awe, fear, trembling, and shuddering"—"for seemingly it is not understood what this comparison is, 'just as there, so too here,'" how is it possible to compare "the Torah study of every person when he learns by himself" to "the Standing at Mount Sinai"—"for even the Torah study of every person and at every time is the word of Hashem literally, as it was said to Moshe at Sinai... as if he received it today from Mount Sinai."

**13.** And it can be said that this is also the explanation in the words of the *Midrash* regarding the giving of the Torah to Yisroel:
"A parable to a king who had an only daughter. One of the kings came and took her. He sought to go to his land and take his wife. He said to him: 'My daughter, whom I gave to you, is an only child. To separate from her I cannot; to say to you, "Do not take her," I cannot, for she is your wife. Rather, do me this favor: wherever you go, make one room for me so that I may dwell among you, for I cannot leave my daughter.' Thus the Holy One, blessed be He, said to Yisroel: 'I gave you the Torah; to separate from it I cannot; to say to you, "Do not take it," I cannot. Rather, wherever you go, make one house for Me so that I may dwell within it.'"

And this matter must be explained regarding the study of Torah—that even when Yisroel study the Torah as it descends and is clothed *in human intellect*, one must make a place (one house) for the dwelling of the Holy One, blessed be He, by the fact that it should be recognized and felt by them that this is *the Torah of the Holy One, blessed be He*, His wisdom and will, may He be blessed, which is why "just as there it was with awe, fear, trembling, and shuddering, so too here it must be with awe, fear, trembling, and shuddering."

**14.** The question is therefore asked—how does a Jew approach the study of Torah:
Knowing that the Torah (even in its being below) is the only daughter of the Holy One, blessed be He—how does he dare in his soul, and especially knowing his status and situation, to approach ("*tzutretn*") the only daughter of the Holy One, blessed be He, and how does he take upon himself to "support" ("*oishhaltn*") the only daughter of the Holy One, blessed be He, together with her Father, the Holy One, blessed be He ("*ir mitn shver tsuzamen*")?!

The answer to this is in the blessing of the Torah—that its opening is "Who chose us from all the nations":
It is not our fault... rather, the Holy One, blessed be He, "chose us"—(even) the body of the Jewish person—"from all the nations."
And as the Holy One, blessed be He, announced through the prophet Malachi: "Was not Esav a brother to Yaakov? ... Yet I loved Yaakov, and Esav I hated." That is to say, the reason for "and I loved Yaakov" is not from the side of the merits of Yisroel, and in the words of the verse, "Not because you were more numerous than all the nations did Hashem desire you, etc.," for, "Was not *Esav a brother to Yaakov*?" Rather, from the side of the essential choice that is in His Essence, may He be blessed, it became "and I loved Yaakov," and automatically, "and Esav I hated."

And because "He chose us from all the nations," therefore, "He gave us His Torah," and from the side of the fact that the Holy One, blessed be He, chose us and gave us His Torah, we approach the study of Torah.

**15.** (The Rebbe concluded:) We are now standing *at the conclusion* of Simchas Torah, and the time for the *Maariv* prayer is already approaching, but we are adding from the profane to the holy, because the Holy One, blessed be He, gave the power to Yisroel to add from the profane to the holy. One must therefore utilize the last moment of Simchas Torah.
- Regarding Yom Kippur, we find that the last moment is when He atones for the undesirable matters that were done on Yom Kippur itself. And likewise regarding Simchas Torah, that at the last moment one can snatch and complete the matters that one lacked throughout all of Simchas Torah.
Therefore: Say *L’chaim* with warmth ("*zogt a warmen a freilechen L’chaim*"), with a happy *nigun*, and take upon yourselves perseverance and diligence in the study of Torah with fear of Heaven.

***

**16.** It is stated in *Likutei Torah* that on every *Yom Tov* one must receive and absorb internally the matters that one absorbed on this *Yom Tov*, and live with them until the next *Yom Tov*. And especially regarding Simchas Torah, after which the *avodah* of "And Yaakov went on his way" begins—one must certainly "take" the revelations of Simchas Torah for the entire year.
However, when standing at the conclusion of Simchas Torah, and preparing for the *avodah* of "And Yaakov went on his way" throughout the new year, with the acceptance of a good resolution that the new year will be as it should be—a question can arise: Many years have already passed in which he resolved that the new year would be as it should be, and in practice... and since so, what is the benefit in accepting a good resolution regarding the *avodah* of this year?!

The answer to this:
For the doing of every thing there is a reason because of which the thing is done, and the reason is—*the pleasure that one derives* from the thing, because of which he does the thing. From this it is understood that the possibility for undesirable matters is only when *his pleasure* is in not-good matters, but when his pleasure will be in matters of *holiness*, then his conduct will be as it should be.
[It was discussed at length regarding the need for atonement even for unintentional sins (by means of a sin-offering), because an unintentional sin proves that his pleasure is in not-good matters, and to a certain extent—even more than in an intentional one, and likewise in a doubtful prohibition even more than in a certain prohibition (which is why there is a stringency in a guilt-offering of doubt that it must be "a two-year-old" compared to a sin-offering which is only "a *danka*"), and likewise the mediation in the words of the Rambam regarding a guilt-offering of doubt was explained: "A man’s heart is pained over his iniquities, and since he set it aside for a doubt, he resolved in his heart to sanctify it," and nevertheless, "if he sacrificed it outside he is exempt, for the prohibition was not established"—edited by the Rebbe and printed in *Likutei Sichos*, Vol. 3, p. 942 and onwards.]

And regarding our matter: when a Jew acts within himself on Simchas Torah to uproot and eradicate ("*oissraisn*") the pleasure in physical and material matters, then he has no need to fear or be affected by obstacles and delays in going out to the *avodah* of "And Yaakov went on his way," and he will certainly walk his way securely.

***

**17.** (Toward the end of the *farbrengen*, the Rebbe said:)
Before the *Maariv* prayer—I wish to repeat a saying of the Rebbe Rayatz (which has already been published in a "copy"), and afterward you will play the *nigun* "Nie Zhuritzi Klaptzi," and after it the *nigun* of the Alter Rebbe, and afterward you will pray *Maariv*.
The Rebbe said: "Behold, he is standing behind our wall," Moshiach is already standing behind the wall ("*hintern vant*"), one only needs the sense of sight and the sense of hearing, but the reality is that "he is standing behind our wall," and he is coming immediately ("*ot ot halt er bei kumen*").

[The Rebbe instructed to play the *nigun* "Nie Zhuritzi Klaptzi," and in the middle of the *nigun* he stood up to his full height and danced in his place. And afterward he instructed to play the Alter Rebbe’s *nigun* of the four stanzas (and instructed to repeat the fourth stanza ten times).
The Rebbe distributed bottles of wine to *anash* from the outlying towns, for the *farbrengens* that will be held in their places. He also gave a bottle of wine for *farbrengens* in Kfar Chabad and throughout the entire Holy Land.]

**18.** (After *Birkat Hamazon* and the *Maariv* prayer, the Rebbe said:)
Following the verse "And Yaakov went on his way"—it is written, "And the angels of G-d met him, etc., *Machanayim*" (plural), "two camps, that of outside the land that came with him until here, and that of the Land of Yisroel that came to meet him."
- The *avodah* must be done by oneself, only that there are matters in which one needs the help of the "angels of G-d."

(The Rebbe concluded:) May Hashem help that for us it should be fulfilled, "And the angels of G-d met him,"
And the main thing—that we should meet together to greet the face of Moshiach ("*m'zol zich treffn tsuzamen antkegn Moshiachn*"), and the Rebbe will lead us toward Moshiach with kindness and mercy,

## B’s”d. Shabbos Parshas Bereishis, Mevarchim HaChodesh Marcheshvan, 5712

(Unedited transcript)

"And Hashem Elokim took the man and placed him in Gan Eden, to work it and to guard it." We must understand the concept of "to work it" and "to guard it" in Gan Eden. It is understandable that "to work it" refers to adding light; even though Gan Eden is spirituality within physicality, it is still possible to have an increase of light there, and that is the meaning of "to work it"—to draw down additional light into Gan Eden. However, the concept of "to guard it" requires explanation. Guarding is done against something harmful, something corrupting, or something inappropriate. Seemingly, this is not applicable to Gan Eden, which is entirely good and cannot tolerate the existence of evil. This is the reason why, after the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, man was sentenced to be expelled from Gan Eden: because Gan Eden cannot tolerate the existence of evil. If so, what is the meaning of "guarding" in Gan Eden?

This can be understood by prefacing the well-known concept that the entire Seder Hishtalshelus is divided into three categories: Olam (world), Shanah (year/time), and Nefesh (soul). The entire Seder Hishtalshelus is founded upon these, which is why these three are explained in Sefer Yetzirah—they are the foundation of the entire Seder Hishtalshelus. Briefly, the concept of Olam is the category of "place," which consists of the six extremities—the four directions, plus above and below.

Just as it is in physicality, there is a category of "place" in the spirituality that is connected to physicality. Since it is a spirituality that is grasped within physicality—meaning a spirituality that has a grasp and comprehension within physicality—it is understood that this category also possesses the six extremities. This can be understood from the *kochos hanefesh* (soul powers). The soul, even as it is Above, possesses powers: the power of sight, the power of hearing, and the power of movement. The power of sight in the soul as it is Above is as stated, "Although He does not see, [the angels] see Him." When it descends below, its power of sight is only regarding physical things. The same applies to the power of hearing; the power of hearing in the soul Above is that it hears the heavenly proclamations. When it descends below, its power of hearing is only regarding physical matters, but regarding spiritual matters, it lacks the power of hearing. Therefore, to hear the heavenly proclamations, the illumination of the soul within the body is insufficient; one requires the essence of the soul, as explained in many places. Thus, when the soul descends below, its powers change. From this, it is understood that the spirituality that is enclothed in physicality possesses the six extremities. Furthermore, even the spirituality that is not enclothed in physicality also possesses the six extremities. For example, regarding intellect: even though intellect is higher than the category of the six extremities—for in the intellectual point, where the essence is the light of the intellect, there are no extremities—nevertheless, when it is drawn down into comprehension, it possesses extremities. These are the details of the comprehension, which are its extremities. Specifically, these are the six extremities, for the details of the comprehension are the *midos* within the intellect, and the *midos* are six in number. The comprehension conceals the point, and therefore much effort is required to extract the point of essence (the point of light and the point of vitality) from the comprehension as it comes in length and breadth, because the comprehension conceals the point. This is also why *Olam* (world) comes from the word *he'elem* (concealment) and *seter* (hiding), because the aspect of the six extremities conceals the essence of the point of vitality.

The concept of *Nefesh* (soul) is the point of light and vitality that is above the category of details; it is the point of light and vitality that is even above the category of a "general" (*klal*) to the details. This does not mean that the details are not drawn from it, but rather that although all details come from it, the point is not a "general" to the details. A "general" is defined as being a general for the details, and "there is nothing in the general except what is in the particular"—meaning that without the particulars, the concept of a general does not exist, because the entire concept of a general is that it is a general for the particulars. This is not the case with the point of light and vitality; it is a concept unto itself and is not a "general." Rather, it is *b'derech mimila* (automatically) that from it come, first, the category of the general for the particulars, and afterwards, the particulars. But it is a concept unto itself, from which come the general vitality, the particular vitality, and the particular powers.

Since the category of *Nefesh* is above the category of details and is not a general to them, and *Olam* is the category of the six extremities—the category of concealment—how does the connection between the *Nefesh* and the *Olam* (the connection of the soul to the body) occur? It occurs through the category of *ratzo v'shov* (running and returning). The soul enclothes itself in the body, and immediately upon enclothing, it is in a state of *ratzo* (running) away from the body. However, because it feels the intent—that the intent is for it to be in the body—it is in a state of *shov* (returning). Thus, the connection of the soul to the body is not a constant connection, but rather in the manner of *ratzo v'shov*, which is the concept of *Shanah* (time/year).

Just as it is regarding the connection of the soul to the body, where the connection requires *ratzo v'shov* specifically, so too is it regarding the vitality of the soul itself; it is in a state of *ratzo v'shov*. The matter is: the manner of vitality by which the soul enlivens the body is that the body itself becomes alive. It is not that the body remains a dead thing in which a living soul is found, but that the body itself becomes alive. It is not that it enlivens it from the outside, but that it itself becomes alive. The power for this in the soul—to enliven the body so that it itself becomes alive—is because the soul is "alive in essence," and because it is alive in essence, it is alive to enliven, so that the body itself becomes alive. From this it is understood that the expansion of vitality to enliven the body is attached to the "alive in essence" aspect of the soul. Because of this, it has the power to enliven the body in a state of *pnimiyus* (inwardness). Therefore, it is understood that the manner of vitality is specifically in a state of *ratzo v'shov*, for it is a state of internal vitality to enliven the body, and on the other hand, this very thing is because it is attached to its source. Thus, there are two opposing movements in this vitality. If the soul itself, as it is alive in essence, were to shine into the body, the body would be nullified from its existence. And if the body remained in its existence, the soul would have to change, and then it would not be in a state of vitality to the body. Therefore, the manner of vitality is in a state of *ratzo v'shov*.

Just as in the entirety of Creation and Seder Hishtalshelus there are the three levels of *Olam, Shanah, Nefesh*, so too in the *avodah* of man—through which the intent of Creation is completed—there are these three categories. Since the perfection and essence of *avodah* is the love of Hashem, these three categories exist in love as well. When one contemplates the matters that bring about love—that is, when one contemplates the matters arranged before him in a manner appropriate to the powers and senses of his soul—he will feel that *Elokus* is a good thing for him, as it is written, "The closeness of Elokim is good for me," and he will be aroused in love for *Elokus*. However, this category of love is the category of love that is said to "return to the lover," for the love is because it is a good thing for him—"good for me." Thus, it is understood that this love is in the category of a felt existence, and it returns to the lover. This love is the category of *Olam*, for *Olam* is the category of existence. However, there is a higher category of love, a higher level in love, which is the category of *Nefesh* in love. His love for *Elokus* is not because of his feeling that "the closeness of Elokim is good for me," but rather he is drawn to *Elokus* in essence. This means that not only does he not feel his own existence (as in the first way, where his existence is felt and because of that is his love), but he does not even feel the love itself—meaning he does not feel at all that he is loving. Like Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai, who said, "I do not know on which path they are leading me." Seemingly, since Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai occupied himself all his days with love, fear, and the study of Torah, how could he say he did not know on which path, etc.? But the matter is that Rabbi Yochanan ben Zakkai was in a state of total *bitul b'metzius* (nullification of existence). Not only did he not feel his own existence—which is the love based on "the closeness of Elokim is good for me"—but he did not even feel that he was loving. He was in a state of *bitul b'metzius*, and consequently, he did not know if he was loving or [otherwise], for he was in a state of total *bitul b'metzius*. This means it is not that he knows the details of the beloved and because of that he loves, but rather he is drawn in essence to the beloved, and he is in a state of *bitul b'metzius*. Now, in order for a person to come from this love of *bitul b'metzius* to a category of love in revelation—a felt love—the intermediary is the category of *hispaalus* (emotional arousal) in the intellect, which is the intermediary to draw the love from the state of *bitul* into revelation. This is the category of *Shanah* in love, which is the intermediary to draw from the category of *Nefesh* to the category of *Olam*. *Mochin* (intellect) is rest; therefore, in the *hispaalus* of the intellect—which is the matter of feeling—it is already from the matter of the *midos*. However, the feeling in this is the feeling of the goodness of the essence of the thing, not the feeling of what is good *for him*. Therefore, it is an intermediary to draw from the category of love of *bitul b'metzius* to the category of love in revelation.

The difference in *avodah* between these two categories of love is that from the love of *bitul b'metzius*, the existence of evil will never branch out. But in felt love—the category of "there is one who loves"—in the multiplicity of *hishtalshelus*, the existence of evil can branch out from it. Because in this love, he is in a state of partial *yeshus* (selfhood), in the multiplicity of *hishtalshelus*, the existence of evil can branch out from it. As in the matter of "and the host of heaven bows to You," who are nullified to *Elokus*—their bowing is because the *Shechinah* is in the West—yet there are people who bow to the sun. Seemingly, this is wondrous: since they are nullified to *Elokus*, how can there be a matter of idol worship from them? But the matter is that their *bitul* is due to their comprehension, as the Rambam writes that the spheres are possessors of soul, knowledge, and intellect, and due to their comprehension, they are nullified to *Elokus*. Since their comprehension brings about the category of *bitul*, and comprehension is *yesh* (existence), therefore, in their *bitul*, there remains in them at least a partial *yeshus*. Because their *bitul* comes through their comprehension, and comprehension is a category of *yesh*, and because there is in them the matter of partial *yeshus*, even though they are nullified to *Elokus*, nevertheless, in the multiplicity of *hishtalshelus*, it is possible for there to be from this a matter of idol worship—a matter that not only conceals and hides *Elokus*, but is opposed to *Elokus*. All this is because there is in them partial *yeshus*. Likewise, it is also in felt love; because it is in the category of *yesh*—that "there is one who loves"—therefore, in the multiplicity of *hishtalshelus*, the existence of evil can branch out from it. This is not the case with the category of love of *bitul b'metzius*, from which the existence of evil will never branch out. To what is this comparable? To a servant who is nullified to a king and is near the king. If he is in a state of total *bitul* to the king, he cannot bear to be honored in the presence of the king. But if he is in a state of partial *yeshus*, even though he is nullified to the king and does everything he is commanded, he can still bear to be honored in the presence of the king. Likewise, in the love that is in the category of *yesh*, evil can branch out, which is not the case with the love of *bitul b'metzius*.

This is what is meant by "And He placed him in Gan Eden, to work it and to guard it." Gan Eden, even though it is the category of the spirituality of the four physical elements, nevertheless, there can be two modes in it: the category of love of *bitul b'metzius* and the category of "there is one who loves." Therefore, there must be the matter of guarding. This is what is meant by "to work it and to guard it." The ultimate intent is that there be a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed, in the lower worlds—for Him, for His very essence. This is the matter of "to work it"—to draw down additional light into Gan Eden, so that it will be the category of the essence of the *Shechinah* in the lower worlds, and not merely revelations alone. The matter of "to guard it" is that because from the category of felt love, in the multiplicity of *hishtalshelus*, the existence of evil can branch out, this is the matter of guarding against damage and corruption, so that the existence of evil will not come from it. This is achieved through the category of *bitul*, so that automatically, the existence of evil will not come from it.

Likewise, it is also during the time of *Galus* (exile), for because of our sins we were exiled from our land—exile after exile. There must be the *avodah* of "to work it and to guard it." The *avodah* of "to work it" is to draw down additional light, which is that the essence of the *Shechinah* should be in the lower worlds—the category of the essence and being of the *Ein Sof*, may He be blessed—at which point there will be a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed. However, in order for the dwelling place to be a "clean dwelling," a dwelling worthy to dwell in, for this one needs the matter of guarding, so that the existence of evil will not branch out from it. This is the category of *bitul*, at which point the existence of evil will not come from it, which is the matter of "to guard it."

The essence of "to work it" is the *avodah* of *birurim* (refining/clarifying), for the essence of the *avodah* in *birurim* is specifically during the time of *Galus*. Like Adam HaRishon, whose essence of the *avodah* of *birurim* was only after he was sentenced to expulsion, and not in Gan Eden. In Gan Eden, the matter of *birurim* was *b'derech mimila*. As in the days of Shlomo, when the *birurim* were in a manner of rest, so too was it in Gan Eden, and the essence of the *birurim* was specifically outside of Gan Eden. So it is now: the essence of the *birurim* is specifically during the time of *Galus*, through which one draws down the essence of the *Shechinah* into the lower worlds. The essence of the revelation of this will be in the time to come, when the essence of the *Shechinah* will be in revelation in the lower worlds. This is also the connection between the two interpretations of what is written, "And the spirit of Elokim hovered over the face of the waters." One interpretation is that "hovered" (*merachefes*) is the letters of *rafach meis* (288 dead), which are the 288 sparks that are called "dead," for "whoever falls from his level is called dead." The second interpretation is that "the spirit of Elokim" refers to the spirit of Mashiach. The connection between the two interpretations is that through the *avodah* with the 288 sparks—the *avodah* of *birurim*, which is the first interpretation—through this, there will be "the spirit of Elokim hovered," which is the spirit of Mashiach, speedily in our days.

## Sicha of Shabbos Bereishis, Mevarchim Chodesh Mar-Cheshvan, 5712

**Unedited**

1. The Rebbe Rayatz related that on Shabbos Bereishis, the Tzemach Tzedek would customarily take a long time to review the weekly parsha, stating the reason: the way one stands (on Shabbos Bereishis) is how it continues and is drawn out for the entire year ("vi men shtelt zich, azoy geyt es").

Similarly, the Rebbe Rayatz related that the Tzemach Tzedek would customarily review the parsha *Shnayim Mikra V’echad Targum*, with the commentary of Rashi and the commentary of the Ramban, verse by verse—though he did not specify whether he did this on every Shabbos of the year or only on Shabbos Bereishis.

In any event, the *length* of the review of the parsha is a matter pertaining to Shabbos Bereishis, for the reason mentioned: it concerns the manner of standing for the entire year—in a movement of *expansion and spreading out*.

It is understood that this matter also applies to the physical needs of Bnei Yisrael. Since for Bnei Yisrael all matters are according to Torah, the standing in a movement of expansion and spreading out on Shabbos Bereishis regarding the reading of the parsha—the first parsha *in the Torah*—serves as a directive to Hashem for the entire year regarding *all the affairs* of Bnei Yisrael, that they should be in expansion and spreading out.

This is also the reason for the Jewish custom—"a Jewish custom is Torah"—to increase on Shabbos Bereishis in the acquisition of mitzvos and matters of joy more than on other Shabbosim (including Shabbos Mevarchim), as mentioned, that the manner of standing on Shabbos Bereishis affects the entire year.

2. This matter should also be connected with the content of Parshas Bereishis (in addition to it being the first parsha in the Torah): Parshas Bereishis is a general parsha, in which general matters are discussed—the creation of the world, man, etc.—and it also encompasses a very long duration of time (the likes of which we do not find in other parshios of the Torah)—from the beginning of creation until shortly before the Flood, more than fifteen hundred years!

It should be noted that this length of time is also emphasized in the ten generations from Adam to Noach—who are discussed in Parshas Bereishis—who lived longer than all the generations that followed them (including the generations from Noach to Avraham), because they were "sustained by the kindness of Hashem". For the essence and perfection of the matter of being "sustained by the kindness of Hashem" (which is said regarding all twenty-six generations before the Giving of the Torah) refers to the ten generations from Adam to Noach, when the intensity of the illumination of the kindness of Arich Anpin was revealed.

It should be added that since Parshas Bereishis is a general parsha, it is understood that the directives learned from the matters discussed in this parsha—as per the saying of the Alter Rebbe that one must live with the time, with the directives learned from the weekly parsha—are general directives for the entire year.

And likewise regarding the matter of "Hashem Elokim took the man and placed him in the Garden of Eden to work it and to guard it," which is stated in the weekly parsha.

*

3. Maamar beginning "Hashem Elokim took the man, etc."

***

4. It was discussed regarding the matter of "Yaakov went on his way", that the empowerment for this comes from what was stated previously, "Lavan rose early in the morning and kissed his sons and his daughters", which hints at the level of the *Supreme Whiteness* (*Lovan HaElyon*) that is revealed on Yom Kippur ("Lavan... for He will whiten your sins like snow"), and is drawn down in the level of *kissing* (*neshikin*), the revelation of love, to every single Jew—discussed by the Rebbe and printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 15, p. 259 and onwards. At the conclusion of the matter, he said:

After this preparation ("Lavan rose early, etc."), the matter of "Yaakov went on his way" is accomplished in such a way that "the angels of Elokim encountered him... Machanayim," "two camps, one of the Diaspora... and one of Eretz Yisrael". That is, he is already standing on the border of Eretz Yisrael, and in one moment and one instant—including "sha'ah" in the sense of turning, "az er git zich nor a ker" (when he just makes a turn)—he is found—together with all the *birurim*—in *Eretz Yisrael*, an entry into the land in its completeness, in a standing and state of complete Redemption. For were it not for the matter of "Yaakov sent messengers," that he did not rely on the help and assistance from Above but sent messengers himself, the entry into the land would have been accomplished then in its completeness.

And likewise in the *avodah* of every single Jew—after the revelations of Yom Kippur (Supreme Whiteness) as they are drawn down internally during the festival of Sukkos and Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah, we are already standing on the border of Eretz Yisrael, ready for the entry into the land in its completeness, in the true and complete Redemption—a *kal v'chomer* from what is explained in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* regarding the blessing of "Forgive us" which we say every day, that "if we had not returned and sinned, we would have been redeemed immediately, as we bless, 'Blessed are You, Hashem, Who redeems Israel'."

Consequently, even when one goes out to the *avodah* of "Yaakov went on his way"—"Yaakov" specifically, *yud-akev* (the heel), and "went on *his* way" specifically, the *avodah* of *birurim* in the affairs of the world, the essence of which is during the time of exile,

—as discussed above that just as for Adam HaRishon the *avodah* of *birurim* had to be specifically outside the Garden of Eden, which is why he was judged with expulsion, so too the essence of the *avodah* of *birurim* is specifically during the time of exile—

one must know that one is standing on the border of Eretz Yisrael, and it is within one's power and ability, in one moment and one instant, to enter Eretz Yisrael in the true and complete Redemption—by revealing the point of the inner heart (bringing it out of exile and captivity), which is the matter of the Redemption and the coming of Moshiach within each and every Jew (as the Alter Rebbe explains). Consequently, when he reveals the point of his own inner heart, and all Bnei Yisrael do the same, they will then bring about the general Redemption with the coming of Moshiach in actual reality.

[The Rebbe instructed that the guests who are fulfilling "Yaakov went on his way" literally, returning to their places of residence after Shabbos ("nit oom Shabbos geredt"), should say "L'chaim," saying that they need to take "provisions for the way."]

***

5. Continuing what was discussed above (Section 4) regarding the matter of "Lavan rose early in the morning and kissed, etc.," the revelation of love that is in the matter of the kissing—it should be added:

It is written, "For Israel is a youth (*na'ar*) and I love him," and the Rebbe (Rashab) explains in his maamar beginning "Zeh",

—this maamar was "placed" for him ("es hot zich bei im geleygt") at the time he said it, without prior preparation—

that generally, "love returns to the lover... for what he loves in another is *self-love*... and as we see in the love of children, that this is because they belong *to him*, and only for his children who belong to him is the love in intensity and revelation; if so, this is self-love. But for a *youth* (*katan*), we see that there is love for all, even if he is not his son, and it is understood from this that this is not because of self-love, but rather it is an essential matter that exists in the essence of love for a youth. And likewise Above, it is written, 'For Israel is a *youth*,' and therefore 'I love him,' which is the matter of essential love"—a love that does not return to the lover, but is from the side of the *beloved*.

From this it is understood that in order to bring about the revelation of the essential love of Hashem, every person must place and position himself ("areinshteln zich") in a standing and state of *smallness*—"*na'ar* (youth) Yisrael" specifically.

And this matter is within the ability of every single Jew:

Regarding matters of *greatness*—there are matters in which everyone can place and position themselves; for example, regarding doing work on Tisha B'Av, it is said, "A person should always make himself a Torah scholar," to desist from his work; and there are also matters regarding which they say, "Not everyone who wishes to take the name may take it", "it appears as arrogance".

But regarding matters of *smallness*—everyone can place and position themselves in such a state, without the need for lengthy contemplation and many calculations... And furthermore, even those who belong to matters of greatness can and must position themselves in a state of smallness, as we find that "even though the righteous have their good deeds to rely upon, they do not ask of the Almighty except as a free gift."

According to this, it can be said that this is also the matter of "he kissed his sons" (his grandchildren)—the *small* ones specifically—to whom the essential love is revealed (similar to "For Israel is a *youth* and I love him").

And this essential love is the empowerment for "Yaakov went on his way,"

—and it should be added that here too "Yaakov" is emphasized specifically, *yud-akev* (not the name of the level, "Yisrael"), which indicates a standing and state of *smallness*. That is, it is in "Yaakov" specifically that the essential love of "*na'ar* Yisrael and I love him" is revealed—

to walk his way securely, knowing that from the side of the revelation of essential love, all the measurements and limitations, concealments and hidings, in everything connected to his *avodah* in fulfilling the Divine intent will certainly be nullified, and it will certainly be (not only with kindness and mercy—for what does that teach us?—but also) with joy and gladness.

(And the Rebbe concluded:) Now it is appropriate to play the *nigun* "Ki V'simcha Tetzei."

[They played the *nigun* "Ki V'simcha Tetzei," and in the middle of the *nigun*, the Rebbe stood to his full height and danced in his place.]

(After the *nigun*, he said:) May it be a happy year ("a freilecher yahr"), and in such a way that one will also see with physical eyes that there is something to be happy about ("az s'iz da fun vos tzu zein freilech"), in both physical and spiritual matters.

## B's"d. Shabbos Parshas Lech Lecha, 11 Marcheshvan, 5712.

[Unedited]
[Following Mincha, the Rebbe spoke about the Rebbe Rashab’s brother, the Raza, whose yahrtzeit (11 Marcheshvan) falls on this Shabbos:]

1. The Rebbe Rashab once spoke about the greatness of his brother the Raza’s humility, saying that such humility was beyond even his own capacity!

2. There are also maamarim of Chassidus by the Raza.
In the library of the Rebbe Rayatz, there are several maamarim of the Raza in his own handwriting. One of them is the maamar beginning with the words "Vayisharnah HaParos," which the Raza delivered in the year 5643 at a wedding that took place in Vitebsk.

- Among the matters that the Rebbe Rayatz desired and wished to bring to print were the maamarim of the Raza, and surely the time will come for this as well.

(The Rebbe concluded:) If we wait to print these maamarim until all the maamarim that have already been printed are studied, I do not know if we will ever be able to print more... Therefore, this should not be a consideration; rather, we must print more and more, and surely, in the end, they will be studied.

## With the help of Hashem. Shabbos Parshas Chayei Sarah, Mevarchim Chodesh Kislev, 5712

(Unedited transcript)

"And the life of Sarah was one hundred years and twenty years and seven years; these were the years of the life of Sarah." The Zohar raises a difficulty: Why is it that here, regarding Sarah, her death is recorded in the Torah, whereas for all other women in the world, their deaths are not recorded in this manner? Rabbi Chiya replied: But is it not written, "And Rachel died," etc.? Rabbi Yossi replied: In all other cases, it is not written in the way it is written regarding Sarah, where it says, "And the life of Sarah was one hundred years and twenty years and seven years." For in all other cases, the days and years are not enumerated as they are for Sarah, and in all other cases, a separate parsha is not written for them as it is for Sarah. The Zohar continues there, stating that when Chava came into the world, she became attached to the *nachash* (serpent), who cast impurity into her, causing death to the world and to her husband. Then Noach came into the world; what is written about him? "And he drank of the wine and became drunk and uncovered himself," etc. Then Sarah came, and she descended and ascended, and did not become attached to him, as it is written, "And Avram went up from Egypt, he and his wife and all that he had." And because Avraham and Sarah did not become attached to him, Sarah merited *chayim ilain* (supernal life) for herself and for her husband, etc. And that is why it says, "And the life of Sarah," for she merited them in all respects, and it is not written for any other woman, "And the life of Chava," and so on for all others; she became attached to *chayim* (life), and therefore, the life was hers.

We must understand this: Since the Zohar’s question is why Sarah is different from all other women in the world (whereas among men, we do find the expression "and the life of..." used, such as for Avraham, Yishmael, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, etc.), why then is the matter of Noach coming into the world, etc., brought up in the continuation? The implication is that this is all one subject—that the corruption of Chava and the corruption of Noach were both rectified by Sarah. We must understand the meaning of this. Furthermore, we must understand why the verse concludes, "the years of the life of Sarah," for seemingly this is a redundancy, after it has already been stated beforehand, "And the life of Sarah was one hundred years," etc.

It is explained in many places regarding the statement about Sarah, "one hundred years and twenty years and seven years," that this indicates that the essential *birur* (refinement) was through Sarah specifically. It is known that the Holy One, Blessed be He, gave the Patriarchs a foretaste of the World to Come in this world. And since it is written regarding the future, "a woman shall encompass a man," meaning that the superiority of the receiver over the giver will be revealed, therefore, this concept was revealed among the Patriarchs, in that the Matriarchs were on a higher level than the Patriarchs. This is what is said regarding Sarah—who is the first of the four Matriarchs—"Whatever Sarah tells you, listen to her voice," because Sarah was on a higher level than Avraham. According to this, the meaning of "one hundred years and twenty years and seven years," stated specifically regarding Sarah, is explained: because in Sarah specifically, there was a revelation of all the levels. And this is what is meant by "one hundred years," which refers to the level of *Keter*, for the level of *Keter* is the first revelation of the existence of light outside of the *Atzmut* (Essence), which is the highest level of revelation. This is the concept of "one hundred years," as is known in numerology that hundreds refer to *Keter*. And even though sometimes the number one thousand, ten thousand, etc., also refers to *Keter*, that is *Keter* as it is in itself; but the level of *Keter* as it becomes the root and source for the emanated beings—that is, the level of *Arich*—is in the number one hundred. For the number one hundred is ten included in ten, which is the perfection of the emanated beings. This is not as *Keter* is in the state of a point, but as it is in the state of a *partzuf* which contains the concept of one hundred. Yet, at the same time, it says "one hundred *shanah*" (year), in the singular (and not "one hundred *shanim*" [years]), because *Keter* is the intermediary between the Emanator and the emanated beings, and every intermediary must contain both of the aspects between which it mediates: the lowest aspect of the higher and the highest aspect of the lower. The concept of the "hundred" in *Keter* is the highest aspect of the emanated beings, as mentioned above that the number one hundred is the perfection of the emanated beings. And the concept of "year" refers to the lowest aspect of the Emanator; for the fact that it is called a "year" indicates that it has a connection to the category of time, and therefore it is the lowest aspect of the Emanator, but nevertheless, it is still within the Emanator, and therefore it is said as "year" in the singular.

Then, this matter is drawn down further below; this is what is meant by "and twenty years." "Twenty" refers to *Chochma* and *Binah*, which do not possess the perfection of ten times ten, and therefore they are in the number of twenty only, which are included in ten only once. As the simple meaning goes, the *mochin* (intellects), which are in the category of apprehension, already have a connection to the existence of *yesh* (somethingness) (unlike *Keter*). Nevertheless, even here it says "year" in the singular, because the *mochin* are the beginning of the formation of the existence of *yesh*, and it is known that the formation of *yesh* is by the power of the *Atzmut* specifically, for He alone has the power and ability to create *yesh me'ayin* (something from nothing). And since in this aspect the *Atzmut* is revealed, therefore it is said as "year" in the singular (for the *Atzmut* is above all division, and above even the aspect of "one" and "unique," etc.). And afterwards it is written, "and seven years," which refers to the level of the *Midos* (emotions), through which the worlds are governed, as it is written, "Remember Your mercies, Hashem, and Your kindnesses, for they are from of old." And because the governance of the worlds is through a multiplicity of lines, as it is stated in the Midrash that if the world were created from the aspect of *Chesed* alone, there would be many sins, and if it were from the aspect of *Gevurah* alone, the world could not exist, therefore there must be a multiplicity of lines, including the *Sefirah* of *Tiferes*, which is the connecting intermediary, and up to all seven *Midos*. Therefore, it says "seven years" in the plural, because in this matter there is the concept of division. This is what is said regarding Sarah: "one hundred years and twenty years and seven years," because since the essential *birur* was through Sarah (as mentioned above, that she was greater than Avraham), therefore she acted in all the levels, from the beginning of all, the level of *Keter*, down to the level of "seven years." According to all this, it is even more difficult: what is the meaning of the conclusion, "the years of the life of Sarah," for what does this add?

To understand all this, we must first preface what is written, "Serve Hashem with joy," that the service of Hashem must be specifically from joy. To the point that the matter of joy is one of the foundations of service, and service without joy is not called service. This is what is written, "Because you did not serve Hashem your God with joy and a good heart... therefore you shall serve your enemies," meaning that even though there was service of Hashem and in perfection, nevertheless, since it was without joy, therefore the punishment of "you shall serve your enemies" is incurred. Seemingly, this is very difficult: since there was service of Hashem in perfection, only the matter of joy was missing, the lack of joy should only cause a reduction in reward, but not a punishment. From this, it is proven that joy is essential in the service of Hashem, and therefore when the matter of joy is missing, it is as if he did not perform his service at all, and therefore a punishment is incurred. We also find in the writings of the Arizal that all the levels the Arizal merited were specifically through the joy of a *mitzvah*.

The explanation of this is that the ultimate intention is what the Holy One, Blessed be He, desired: to have for Himself a dwelling place in the lower worlds. A dwelling place means the drawing down of the *Atzmut* of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He. And the drawing down of the *Atzmut* is specifically through joy, and not through understanding and apprehension. For through understanding and apprehension, one grasps only this aspect of *Elokus* (Divinity) as it is grasped in understanding and apprehension, and it is specifically through joy that one reaches the *Atzmut*. An example of this is in the service of prayer, which is the essential service, as the Sages say, "What is the service of the heart? This is prayer." There are two aspects in prayer: the contemplation of *Elokus* in prayer, and the delight and joy in *Elokus* in prayer. Although the delight and joy in *Elokus* come after and through the contemplation, this is only because the contemplation is merely a vessel for the joy and delight; for when one understands and grasps the thing, this causes delight and joy. Nevertheless, they are distinct in their matters and in their roots. The matter of contemplation does not have the ability to grasp the *Atzmut*, for the intellect of the lower is not at all in proportion to the intellect of the higher. As it is in all matters among created beings, which are not in proportion to the *Atzmut*, as is explained regarding what Avraham said, "And I am dust and ashes," that the *Middah* of *Chesed* of Avraham is in the state of dust and ashes relative to the *Middah* of *Chesed* of above. And all the more so in a person who prays, whose intellect is not at all in proportion to the level of the intellect of above. The fact that the lower intellect is derived from the higher intellect is by way of a change of essence, as in the matter of the *Midos*; this is why the *Middah* of *Chesed* of Avraham Avinu is in the state of dust and ashes relative to the *Middah* of *Chesed*, because the matter of ashes indicates a change of essence. Not so through the delight and joy in prayer, through which one grasps the *Atzmut*, for in the matter of delight and joy, the level of the delight of above is drawn down literally. This is similar to what is explained regarding the descent of the *Kesarim* (crowns) one from another, that even though there are differences in levels between the *Keter* of one world and the *Keter* of the world below it, nevertheless they are derived one from another, and everything is one matter. For the light which is the aspect of *Memalei Kol Almin* (filling all worlds), the manner of its drawing down below is through a change of essence, unlike the aspect of *Ohr Sovev* (surrounding light), the aspect of *Igulim* (circles), the aspect of *Keter* and *Makif* (surrounding), for everything is one matter. This is what is achieved through the joy and delight that one rejoices in *Elokus* and delights in his soul; through this, one reaches the aspect of the *Atzmut* of the *Ohr Ein Sof*.

The vessel for the matter of joy in *Elokus* is *bitul* (nullification), for in a place where there is *bitul*, there is the revelation of the supernal joy, unlike in the feeling of *yesh* (somethingness), where the matter of joy does not exist. This is what is written, "And the humble shall increase joy in Hashem," for the humble specifically increase joy in Hashem. Seemingly, this is wondrous (as is also explained in the *Maamar* "And the humble shall increase" by the Rebbe Rayatz), for humility and joy are two opposite movements: humility is the movement of contraction, and joy is the movement of expansion and broadening; how is it possible that through humility a person can reach joy? But the matter is that humility is not the self-abasement that comes from a low opinion of the soul, where one finds no good in himself, but rather the matter of humility is from the absence of self-feeling. Even though he knows his own merits, he does not consider himself a "something." It is not that he does not know of his good; rather, he knows he is good and upright in every matter, but nevertheless, he does not take credit for himself, because he is essentially nullified. Furthermore, when he contemplates that all his good is not from himself but comes as an inheritance from our ancestors—just as he believes in Hashem and is attached to Hashem with attachment and love, etc.—it is known that faith is an inheritance for us from Avraham Avinu, and likewise the love in the soul of every Jew is an inheritance from Avraham, and included in this is also *yirah* (awe) and all other merits. From this comes humility, since it is not by his own power. This is what is said regarding Moshe, "And the man Moshe was very humble, more than any man on the face of the earth," even though he knew his good, etc., because this is what was given to him as a gift from above, and he thought that if these powers were in another, he would also be on this level, and furthermore, it is possible that he would have revealed the powers even more than he did. And this humility is a vessel for the matter of joy. For the matter of joy comes specifically when one receives a gift that he did not earn and that is not due to him, and therefore he is joyful; but when one receives his reward, there is no room for joy over it. Therefore, one who does not have the *Middah* of humility, but feels his own merit, his joy (over the things he received) is not in perfection, firstly because he thinks the thing is due to him, and furthermore, if he lacks some details, the lack causes sadness. But specifically one who has the *Middah* of humility, who is nullified in himself—meaning that even though he knows his own merit, he is in *bitul* as mentioned above—because he knows that his merits did not come to him through his own toil, and furthermore, he thinks that another would be better than him if they were given these merits, then his joy over everything he has is in perfection, for he knows that it is not due to him, and furthermore, if he lacks some details, this does not cause sadness as mentioned above.

However, even though true joy comes through humility and *bitul*, in this joy itself there can be several modes. Sometimes it is possible that the joy itself is in a felt manner. True joy is simple joy in *Elokus* in such a way that he does not feel himself at all, for he forgets about himself entirely, and therefore he does not feel how the thing is good for him, but it is *Elokis* joy without self-feeling. But when the matter of joy is felt by him, then the supernal joy departs, and it is even possible that he could fall into evil, Heaven forbid. And even though the feeling is subtle, still, from this, there can be nourishment for the *chitzonim* (external forces). After prayer, this could lead to haughtiness, etc. This is the matter of "and his concubine, whose name was Reumah," as the explanation is known, that *Reumah* is the letters of *Re'u Mah* (see what), and she is the aspect of the *Kelipat Nogah* of *Atzilus*, meaning that she is in the aspect of *bitul*, the aspect of *Mah* (what), but the *bitul* itself is in a felt manner, that the *bitul* is seen and felt, and she says "see what," see that I am nullified. And so it is in the matter of joy; since the matter of joy is the absence of limitation and the ultimate expansion—as is known that joy breaks through barriers—from this, through a multiplicity of descent, there can be a matter of nourishment, etc. For in *Atzilus*, where "no evil shall dwell with You," the matter of *Kelipat Nogah* is that the *bitul* is felt. But from this is drawn down afterwards, through a multiplicity of descent, the matter of *Kelipat Nogah* of *Asiyah*, which is an intermediary to absolute evil. And so it is in the matter of joy: when the joy is felt, it is possible that from this will emerge a matter of absolute evil, just as one who is an evil person by essence, at the time of joy, his barrier is broken and his *yeshus* (selfhood) and wickedness are revealed to all. But when a person is in the aspect of *bitul* by essence, then specifically at the time of joy, his *bitul* comes to revelation, that he waives his honor and connects with every person, etc. And this is why the perfection of joy is when even the joy itself is not felt at all, for specifically then the delight that is in the *Atzmut* is drawn into this joy, and it is impossible for there to be any nourishment from this for the *chitzonim* at all.

The order of service as it was from the side of Creation was in the manner of true joy that comes through humility and *bitul*. "The world was created in its fullness," and therefore the matter of the service of Hashem was also in its perfection, in the aspect of joy, and in a manner that this was relevant to everyone, since joy is not merely a matter of adornment. But through the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, a blemish was made in the matter of joy. It is known that the sin of the Tree of Knowledge was in the matter of feeling, as it is written, "And the woman saw that the tree was good for food, and that it was a desire to the eyes, and the tree was desirable to make wise," meaning that the sin was in that all matters should be in feeling. It is stated in the writings of the Arizal that before the sin, Adam HaRishon's head was in *Beriah*, his body in *Yetzirah*, and his feet in *Asiyah*, and from this it is understood that the intention in this matter of "and that it was a desire," etc., is nothing but for feeling in spiritual matters. But the sin in this was that Adam HaRishon wanted *Elokus* to be in a felt manner, as it is stated in *Rabbeinu Bachya* that he wanted to "make wise," and the meaning of the words is that even before this, he had intellect, but it was *Elokis* intellect only, without feeling, and the sin was in that he wanted the intellect to be in a felt manner. And after the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, it is impossible for the matter of joy in the service of Hashem to be in perfection for everyone, because there is the matter of feeling as mentioned above, from which there can be nourishment for the *chitzonim*. And it is impossible for the matter of joy to be in revelation except in great *tzaddikim*. But for all other people, the matter of joy must be only in the interior, but in the exterior, there is the matter of *yirah* (awe) specifically. This is what is written, "And rejoice with trembling," for "rejoice" indicates hidden joy, and in revelation is the matter of trembling, *bitul*, and acceptance of the yoke. And even though seemingly it is wondrous how it is possible to have a connection of these two matters at once, joy and trembling together, the explanation of this is known, that this is like the parable of the servant who serves his master with the ultimate acceptance of the yoke, that he is not a "something" for himself at all, and therefore he also has delight, but his delight is the delight of the master. Meaning, that since he is not a "something" for himself, he is not relevant to any feeling at all, and therefore it is not relevant that he should have any delight from himself in his service, but nevertheless, the perfection of the acceptance of the yoke is that since the master delights and rejoices in the service of the servant, therefore the servant himself also delights and rejoices from this, for it is not his own delight and joy, but it is the delight and joy of the master. And so it is also in the subject of the service of man, that the service itself is by way of acceptance of the yoke, but together with this, there is the delight and joy over the completion of the supernal intention of making a dwelling place for Him, blessed be He, in the lower worlds.

In all this, one can understand what is written in the Zohar there, "Noach came into the world," etc., "Sarah came into the world," etc. We stated above that the sin of the Tree of Knowledge is that the matter of feeling was created. And this is the matter of what the *nachash* (serpent) came upon Chava and cast impurity into her, meaning the matter of feeling that is in every thing. It can be said that this is also the reason why, after the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, the manner of refining the sparks is by way of *hitlabshut* (enclothement) and not by way of *mimila* (automatically). As is known regarding the matter that after the sin, Adam HaRishon was driven out of the Garden of Eden, as it is written, "And Hashem God sent him from the Garden of Eden to work the ground from which he was taken," that after the sin, the manner of refining the sparks is through the service in them by way of *hitlabshut*. For before the sin, the refinement was by way of *mimila*, that the light shone in its place and the sparks were elevated and included in it by way of *mimila*, as it was in the days of Shlomo, when "the moon stood in its fullness," when there was then a refinement of the sparks by way of *mimila*. But through the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, the corruption was made, and the refinement must be by way of *hitlabshut*. It can be said that this is connected with what we stated above, that after the sin, the service is in a felt manner specifically.

Noach wanted to rectify this sin through his service. This is what is written regarding Noach, "And he planted a vineyard," etc., the matter of wine, that through this he wanted to rectify the matter of feeling. For wine is the aspect of *Binah* and apprehension, and it is known that in apprehension there are two modes: the apprehension of the positive and the apprehension of the negative. The apprehension of the positive is when one apprehends the thing itself, in such a way that the intellect grasps and encompasses the apprehended object, and the apprehended object is grasped in the intellect, and this means that the intellect does not go out of its boundary and place, but it grasps the apprehended object as it is. And the matter of the apprehension of the negative is that he does not know the thing at all, and his knowledge is only in the wonderment of the thing, but he does not recognize the thing at all, and even the wonderment he does not recognize and apprehend, but he knows that the thing is wondrous. And this is the matter of the nullification of apprehension, that he goes out of his apprehension. And this is the matter of *Chochma* and the interior of *Binah*. This is what Noach wanted to rectify the sin of the Tree of Knowledge through the aspect of wine, the interior of *Binah*, meaning through the *bitul* that is in the apprehension of the negative. However, from the side of the matters that were then, he did not succeed, and on the contrary, he became confused; this is what is written, "And he became drunk," etc., for drunkenness indicates confusion. The reason for this is because even though he was in *bitul*, nevertheless, this is *bitul* of apprehension and not *bitul* entirely.

However, afterwards, Sarah came into the world, and she descended and ascended, and did not become attached to him, for there was not in her the matter of the impurity that was in the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, for Sarah specifically was able to rectify the corruption that was in the sin of the Tree of Knowledge. The matter is that the innovation of the service of Sarah is the *bitul* of acceptance of the yoke, which is above the *bitul* of apprehension mentioned above, meaning that she drew down the *bitul* of acceptance of the yoke also in the service that is in a felt manner. For in the Zohar there, it is implied that the innovation is in that Sarah specifically went down to Egypt and went up from there, "she descended and ascended." The reason for this is that the fact that Avraham went up from Egypt is not so wondrous, for the matter of Avraham is *Yirah Ila'ah* (supernal awe), which is what Avraham is, the letters of *Eiver Mah* (the limb of "what"), the aspect of *bitul* in existence, the *bitul* of *Chochma*. And in this, there is not so much of an innovation in that he went up from there. But Sarah, whose matter is *Shem Ben* (the Name *Ben*), the aspect of *bitul* of *yesh*, *Yirah Tata'ah* (lower awe), in this is the innovation, that the matter of the impurity of the sin of the Tree of Knowledge did not become attached to her, meaning that she drew down this *bitul* also in a felt manner. For the difference between *Yirah Ila'ah* and *Yirah Tata'ah* is that *Yirah Ila'ah* is *bitul* in existence, and *Yirah Tata'ah* is the aspect of *bitul* of *yesh*, meaning that he is a *yesh* and nevertheless he is nullified. But in *Yirah Tata'ah* itself, there are two modes. It is possible to have the matter of *bitul* of *yesh* from the side of apprehension, like in Noach, where the *bitul* was from the side of apprehension (the apprehension of the negative), and there is the matter of the *bitul* of acceptance of the yoke, which is absolute *bitul*, until the aspect of *bitul* in existence of *Yirah Ila'ah* is drawn into it. And this is what was drawn into Sarah from Avraham, because she was with Avraham, that she drew down the *bitul* in existence also in the aspect of *Shem Ben*, the *bitul* of *yesh*, until she drew down this *bitul* also in a felt manner. It can be said that the reason this matter was acted upon by Sarah (and not by Noach) is because then there was already the beginning of the revelation of the Giving of the Torah, "two thousand years of Torah," and therefore Sarah, through her service, was able to rectify the corruption of the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, to draw down the *bitul* also in a felt manner.

In all this, one can understand why the verse concludes and repeats "the years of the life of Sarah." The matter is that after the verse explains the matter of "one hundred years," the aspect of *Atik* and *Arich* (*Keter*, as mentioned above), and "twenty years," *Chochma* and *Binah*, and "seven years," *ZON* (*Ze'er Anpin* and *Nukvah*), the innovation of Sarah is that the supernal *bitul* is drawn down also to the very lowest levels in the worlds of *Beriah*, *Yetzirah*, and *Asiyah*, and as mentioned above, that she drew down the *bitul* also in a felt manner. And this is the general matter of the service of man, which must be "and rejoice with trembling," as mentioned above, meaning that the service itself is in acceptance of the yoke, in trembling, and like a servant whose essential service is in acceptance of the yoke (for "a servant is comfortable with lawlessness"), and in this itself there is the matter of joy, that the servant rejoices and delights in the delight and joy of the master, for then the matter of acceptance of the yoke is drawn down also in the joy that is in a felt manner. And regarding this, it is stated in the Zohar there, "the life was hers," for specifically in this matter, the *chayim ilain* (supernal life) of above are drawn down.
