And in two ways: (a) the bond of the "hidden" of Hashem, Torah, and Israel between them, and the bond of the "revealed" of Hashem, Torah, and Israel between them, (b) the bond of the hidden of Hashem with the revealed of Hashem, the revealed of Hashem with the hidden of Torah, the hidden of Torah with the revealed of Torah, the revealed of Torah with the hidden of Israel, and the hidden of Israel with the revealed of Israel,

And in every way—in the "revealed" of Israel, while they are in this physical world, the "hidden" of Hashem, the essence and being of the *Ein Sof* *Baruch Hu*, is also continued and revealed.

And all this is continued and revealed in this physical and material world, that in it is made the revelation of "Hashem is One and His Name is One," "When I am written I am read" (unlike in this time that *Havayah* is written and *Adnut* is read), and up to the revelation of the *power of the essence* that is in the creation of something from nothing, as the Alter Rebbe explains in *Iggeres HaKodesh* that "the being and essence of the Emanator, may He be blessed, whose existence is from His essence and is not caused by any cause that preceded Him, *chas v'shalom*... He alone has the power and ability to create something from nothing and absolute nothingness, without any other cause and reason preceding this 'something'."

And so it will be for us—through the service of the connection of hidden and revealed [in the path of the Alter Rebbe who opened and paved for each one of us, and showed not only that we can walk in it, but also how to walk in it, so that this is in the power of each one of us], that each one will connect the hidden and revealed within him (in Israel), through this there will be for him the connection of hidden and revealed in the Torah, for then the connection of hidden and revealed of Hashem also acts, and consequently, also the hidden end, "the heart to the mouth is not revealed," is continued and revealed below ten *tefachim*, and we merit the complete and true Redemption speedily in our days.

***

**16.** It was discussed several times about the need for reviewing Chassidus in *shuls*.

And the reason for this is because of the benefit that is in the matter—and in two: (a) for the *bochurim* themselves, that in order to review Chassidus by heart, they will need by necessity to study Chassidus themselves (for it is impossible to review without studying beforehand...). (b) for the *baalei-batim* who are in the *shuls*.

And now, regarding the first benefit, the study of Chassidus and the knowledge of Chassidus—there are those among the *yungeleit* (young married men) and all the more so the *baalei-batim* who are already "advanced in years" who think that they do not need this benefit, since the teachings of Chassidus are for them "as if placed in a box"... and they only need to "air out" the matters from time to time, a matter that is not involved with effort at all,

But, to *exert* themselves to study the *maamar* by heart, and afterwards to go to *shul* and review it—they are not

## B’s”d. Shabbos Parshas Va’era, 28 Teves, Mevarchim HaChodesh Shevat, 5712

(Unedited transcript)

"And Elokim spoke to Moshe and said to him, 'I am Hashem. And I appeared to Avraham, to Yitzchak, and to Yaakov as Kel Shaddai, but by My name Hashem I was not known to them.'" Further on in the verses, it is stated: "And I will take you out," "and I will rescue," "and I will redeem," "and I will take"—four expressions of redemption—"and you shall know that I am Hashem." The implication is that it was specifically through the redemption from Mitzrayim that they arrived at the knowledge of the name Hashem. 

We must understand this, for we find that the name Hashem was revealed to the Patriarchs as well, as it is written: "And Hashem appeared to Avram," "And Hashem appeared to him," and the like. If so, what is meant by "but by My name Hashem I was not known to them"? Furthermore, we must understand why they merited this level specifically through the exodus from Mitzrayim, the redemption from Mitzrayim. This implies that it was specifically because they were in the exile of Mitzrayim and were redeemed from it that they merited the revelation of the name Hashem. It is impossible to say that the revelation of the name Hashem is only because they were no longer in the exile of Mitzrayim, for the Patriarchs were also not in exile, yet "by My name Hashem I was not known to them." This proves that the intent of the verse is that specifically through having been in the exile of Mitzrayim and being redeemed from it, they arrived at the revelation of "and you shall know that I am Hashem." We must understand the concept here.

All of this can be understood by prefacing the teaching of our Sages: "If Yisrael repent, they are redeemed; and if not, they are not redeemed." This implies that teshuvah is not only necessary if there is sin and iniquity, but that in any case, it is impossible for the redemption to occur without teshuvah. The Rambam also rules that Yisrael are only redeemed through teshuvah, and the term "if not" implies a condition for the redemption. We must understand the necessity for teshuvah to precede the redemption. It is understandable that if there is sin and iniquity, teshuvah is required for them before the future redemption, for regarding the future it is written, "And I will remove the spirit of impurity from the earth," and therefore there must first be a nullification of sins and iniquities so that the *sitra achra* has no hold on a person in his thoughts, speech, and action. But when there are no sins, why is teshuvah necessary?

The matter is as follows: Regarding the teshuvah (which Yisrael are destined to perform at the end of their exile), it is written, "For no one cast away shall be cast away from Him"—"from Him" specifically, referring to the *Atzmus* of the Holy One, blessed be He, for all the sparks in all the souls of Yisrael will ultimately be drawn into the "Body of the King," the *Atzmus* of the Holy One, blessed be He. But how can this soul, which is in the category of a limited and created being, be drawn into the "Body of the King," the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*, who is in the category of the Infinite and the Creator? Moreover, it is truly impossible to even apply the term "Infinite" to Him, just as it is impossible to say that He is in the category of "limited," for the *Atzmus* is the negation of limitation and the negation of the infinite, the negation of affirmation and the negation of negation. If so, it is all the more wondrous how the soul can be connected with the *Atzmus*, when the soul is in the category of limitation at the very opposite end, especially when it is clothed in a body.

The matter is that the connection is through Torah and mitzvos. The Torah is the wisdom and will of the Holy One, blessed be He, and the mitzvos are the "limbs of the King." Nevertheless, they have descended and devolved from their place of glory and are clothed in physical matters. Regarding the Torah, our Sages said that when the angels requested that the Torah be given to them, the response to their request was, "Have you gone down to Mitzrayim? Is there an evil inclination among you?" The fact that this matter was raised regarding the giving of the Torah (and not only the performance of mitzvos) proves that the Torah itself was clothed in physical things. This is also true of the mitzvos in a simple sense, as the mitzvos are performed with physical objects. Even the mitzvos whose fulfillment is in the mind and heart, the measure of the mitzvah is that it be felt in the physical brain and physical heart. Therefore, Torah and mitzvos are the intermediaries that connect and unite the divine soul—which is in the category of limitation and space and is clothed in a body—so that it can be nullified and included in the light of the *Ein Sof*, to be drawn into the "Body of the King," the *Atzmus* of the Holy One, blessed be He. For this reason, the mitzvos are called "garments," as they clothe the soul of man so that it can be included in the light of the *Ein Sof* and "gaze upon the pleasantness of Hashem" and be drawn into the "Body of the King."

This is what is meant by "And Avraham was old, advanced in days," and it is stated in the Zohar on this verse that "advanced in days" means "complete days"—these are the supernal days, which are the garments of Torah and mitzvos. The days are the category of garments to clothe the soul of man, and they are the garments of Torah and mitzvos, through which a person can draw upon himself His unity. This is the meaning of "And Avraham was old, advanced in days"—"old" is one who has acquired wisdom, for the category of wisdom is the revelation of the unity from above, as explained in Tanya, that the category of wisdom is that "He alone is He, and there is nothing else." To reach this level, Avraham was "advanced in days," meaning the garments of Torah and mitzvos. This matter is connected to days in the literal sense, that every day must be filled with the performance of Torah and mitzvos, as the saying goes, "Every single day He performs His work," meaning that every day there must be the performance of the Torah and mitzvos of that day. Through this, it is possible to reach the connection of the soul with the *Atzmus* of the Holy One, blessed be He. Therefore, a person must accumulate Torah and mitzvos, even the same mitzvah many times, according to the number of days given to him from heaven. Furthermore, sometimes one performs the same mitzvah several times in one day, such as the prayers, where there are three prayers every day, four on Shabbos and Yom Tov, and five on Yom Kippur.

One might add: seemingly, this is difficult to understand, for it is known that the merit of the souls is that they are in the category of "walkers," whose service is in the category of movement and ascent from level to level, as explained in the interpretation of the verse, "And I will give you walkers among these who stand." If so, why is it necessary to engage in the same mitzvah several times in one day? But based on the above, it is understood: it is true that the service itself is in the category of ascent from level to level, but the mitzvos are only in the category of garments through which one can connect his soul to *Elokus*. Therefore, one must perform these mitzvos many times so that his soul can be connected with *Elokus*, and then the ascent and movement can take place.

With this, we can explain the contradiction we find regarding the obligation of Torah study. In one place, our Sages said that one who is able to engage in Torah and does not, of him it is said, "For he has despised the word of Hashem... he shall surely be cut off." In another place, they said that one who is unable to engage in Torah all day because of his business, it is sufficient for him to study one chapter in the morning and one chapter in the evening. If we say that the one who neglects Torah study is subject to "he shall surely be cut off" because of the greatness of the Torah—that it is a degradation of the Torah—then why is it sufficient for a businessman to study one chapter in the morning and one in the evening? And if we say that the matter of Torah study depends on the leisure time a person has, so that one who is a businessman is exempt with one chapter in the morning and one in the evening, then what is the outcry if someone who has leisure time neglects it for a short while, to the point that it is said of him "he shall surely be cut off"?

The matter is understood based on what was explained above, that the Torah is a garment for the soul so that it can connect with *Elokus*, to be drawn into the "Body of the King." Therefore, it depends on which soul is being discussed. There is a soul that needs more garments, and there is a soul for whom the need for garments is not as great. Therefore, one who is unable to engage in Torah all day long because of the business of earning a living—since his livelihood was not provided for him from heaven in a way that he would be free all day to engage in Torah—it is proven that his soul does not need the garments of Torah as much, and it is sufficient for him to study one chapter in the morning and one in the evening. But one who is able to engage in Torah all day, it is proven that his soul needs more garments, and therefore he is forbidden to neglect even one moment; rather, he must engage all day according to the measure of garments required for the root of his soul. If not, then "he shall surely be cut off," for his soul cannot ascend and gaze upon the light of Hashem. Proof of this is what our Sages said, that one who neglects the mitzvah of *Krias Shema* even once is as if he did not read it all his days, for since he lacks this garment, he lacks the connection with the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He. It is specifically through the performance of Torah and mitzvos every single day, according to the number of days allotted to him, that the connection of the souls with the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, can occur.

Our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe explains that not every person merits that all his days be complete, without missing even one hour or one moment. One can say in explanation of the precision of the Alter Rebbe's language, "not every person merits," that this implies it is a matter of merit from above, not something that depends on choice. It can be said that this is understood based on the well-known teaching that a person is not saved from *bitul Torah* (neglect of Torah) every day, as implied by our Sages' teaching that there are three sins from which a person is not saved every day. It turns out that this is not something that depends on a person's choice, but requires merit and heavenly assistance. The Alter Rebbe continues that the advice for this is that all his days should be in *teshuvah*. The meaning is: since not every person can merit that there be no deficiency in his garments, and if so, how can a person arrive at the connection of his soul with the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He? The advice for this is through *teshuvah*. For even through *teshuvah* one can come to be drawn into the "Body of the King."

He explains there that *shuvah* (repentance) shares the same letters as *boshah* (shame), and *teshuv* shares the same letters as *boshes* (shame). The concept of *teshuvah* is that one should arrive at "shame-fear," fear resulting from shame. By deepening his intellect in the greatness of Hashem—that He fills all worlds and encompasses all worlds, and everything is as nothing before Him, and the light of the *Ein Sof* is above without end and below without limit—shame before Him, blessed be He, will certainly fall upon him. For even though he loves Hashem and fears Hashem, his love and fear are considered as nothing. As the Tzemach Tzedek brings on this, what the Alter Rebbe wrote in the discourse *U'Taher Libenu* in the name of the Maggid: that the interpretation of "shame-fear" is like the teaching regarding the *Keser Elyon* (Supernal Crown), that even though it is "a bright light, a polished light," it is "black" before the Cause of all causes. When a person is precise with himself and takes to heart how even the *Keser Elyon* of *Atzilus* is "black" and is ashamed before the light of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, then awe and great fear will fall upon him. Especially when a person contemplates that he does not even know the essence of the *Sefiros*, for his knowledge of them is only knowledge of their existence and not the attainment of their essence—and all the more so, he does not know the category of *Keser Elyon*, especially as it is before the *Tzimtzum*, for even the *Keser Elyon* before the *Tzimtzum* is "black" before the Cause of all causes. (This matter applies to all levels within the *Keser Elyon*, for even in its most supernal levels, and even in the level that is above the category of levels entirely, even there it is "black" before the Cause of all causes; on the contrary, the Cause of all causes is found specifically below, as explained elsewhere). Through this contemplation, a person arrives at the category of shame, which is the concept of *teshuvah*. And through *teshuvah*, the connection of the soul with the *Atzmus* of the *Ein Sof*, blessed be He, can occur.

The explanation of the matter is as follows: It is written, "For Yisrael is a youth, and I loved him, and from Mitzrayim I called to My son." The matter is like what we see, for example, with a young boy: as long as he is in proximity to his father and his father shows him his love and draws him near with extra love and affection, the boy becomes emboldened in his soul to do foolish things due to the smallness of his intellect, even if it is against his father's will, and even if his father protests, he does not pay attention to him and does not listen to his voice. Only when his father hides his face from him and pushes him outside, to the point that he tells him he is not his father at all, then specifically the son is awakened to be in his father's proximity. Such is the matter of the love of Yisrael for the Omnipresent, blessed be He, which is hidden in the heart of every single one of Yisrael; it does not emerge from concealment to revelation except through the contemplation of his distance from Hashem. This is "For Yisrael is a youth, and I loved him"—when there is the matter of proximity ("and I loved him"), there can be "Yisrael is a youth," that he does deeds of youth and smallness. And specifically "from Mitzrayim I called to My son"—through Mitzrayim, which is constriction and smallness, the concept of shame mentioned above, through this "I called to My son," for through this is the revelation of love with greater intensity.

More specifically, the matter of the exile of Mitzrayim, through which the revelation of love occurs, is that a person finds himself in his service in a state of descent, which awakens in him even more the feeling of shame and *teshuvah*. Within this itself, there are several levels, as explained in the discourse of the Alter Rebbe, that there is a category of "Mitzrayim of holiness" and a category of "Mitzrayim of the *sitra achra*." The "Mitzrayim of holiness" is that he is satisfied with his Torah and service—he studies Torah and serves Hashem, but does not strive to increase in Torah and good deeds; rather, he is satisfied with what he is engaged in, because in his own eyes he has fulfilled his obligation. One could say that this is also the concept of performing mitzvos as "a commandment of men learned by rote." From the "Mitzrayim of holiness," it descends and devolves until it becomes below in the *kelipah* the category of "Mitzrayim of the *sitra achra*," which is the category of the blemish of the covenant. Sometimes it is against his will, that they defile him against his will through a nocturnal occurrence, as it is written, "which Mitzrayim enslave them." The concept of the exodus from Mitzrayim is the category of *teshuvah* through this very matter, when he sees in himself that he is distant from Hashem in the extreme, for then "from Mitzrayim I called to My son," for the distance specifically awakens in him *teshuvah* and the feeling that he is "My son," and through this he connects his soul with the *Atzmus*, to be drawn into the "Body of the King."

From all this, we can understand the merit of the matter of *teshuvah*: even one whose days are not complete, who lacks in his garments of Torah and mitzvos—for not every person merits this, as mentioned above—it is possible for his soul to be connected with the *Atzmus* through *teshuvah*. On the contrary, there is a merit in the connection through *teshuvah* over the connection through the garments of Torah and mitzvos. The drawing down through the garments of Torah and mitzvos is in the category of limitation, from the level of "filling all worlds." But through *teshuvah*, for *teshuvah* is in a single moment and a single instant, the drawing down through it is without limit. As explained above, the concept of *teshuvah* is shame—that any matter of measurement and limitation he knows is "black" before the Cause of all causes, and he wants to emerge from this limitation. Therefore, the drawing down through *teshuvah*, the category of "from Mitzrayim I called to My son," is a drawing down that is even more exalted.

This is "And I appeared to Avraham, to Yitzchak, and to Yaakov as Kel Shaddai..." The revelation to the Patriarchs is the category of *Kel Shaddai*, which in general is the concept of "filling all worlds." Although there are several categories in *Kel Shaddai*—there is the concept that He said to His world "enough" (*dai*), which is the nature of the world that is in the category of concealment and hiding, and there is the concept of *Kel Shaddai* above this, regarding which it is written, "And I will pour out for you a blessing until there is no *dai*," and our Sages said "until it is sufficient," which is the drawing down of *Elokus* into the worlds—nevertheless, it is only "until it is sufficient" and not the matter of wealth. As is known regarding the matter of "sufficient for his need which he lacks," even a horse to ride upon and a servant to run before him—all this is only the matter of filling a lack and not the matter of wealth and luxury. That is, the drawing down from the category of "filling all worlds." However, specifically through the descent into the exile of Mitzrayim, they arrived at the revelation of the name Hashem—"from Mitzrayim I called to My son"—the drawing down from the category of Hashem, without limit, "and you shall know that I am Hashem."

This is "And Elokim spoke to Moshe and said to him, 'I am Hashem.'" This verse is a response to Moshe's question above, "Why have You done evil to this people?"—that is, why was the whole matter of the exile of Mitzrayim necessary? To this comes the response, "And said to him, 'I am Hashem,'" for the purpose of the exile of Mitzrayim is the revelation of the name Hashem. And although the name Hashem existed also for the Patriarchs as mentioned above, that is the category of Hashem of "below," the category of the name Hashem that pertains to the worlds, Hashem from the root *mehaveh* (bringing into being). However, through the descent of the exile of Mitzrayim, they arrived at the revelation of "and you shall know that I am Hashem" which is above the categories of the world, for Hashem is "He was, He is, and He will be" as one. This matter comes through the service of *teshuvah* as mentioned above, which is what is meant by "And I will give it to you as an inheritance," for the love that comes from the category of *teshuvah* is like an inheritance, where one falls into a great fortune for which he did not labor. So too, the love and closeness to Hashem that comes through *teshuvah* and shame is not through his good deeds day by day (as mentioned above), but in one hour, by way of an inheritance that comes from above. One should add further that the matter of inheritance is because the heir has a relationship to the bequeather, and the state of the heir does not matter in this; therefore, even a deaf-mute, an imbecile, or a minor inherits, because what matters is only that he has a relationship to the bequeather. This is "an inheritance, I am Hashem," for to arrive at the category of Hashem from above is through inheritance. Furthermore, "inheritance" (*morasha*) is also from the root *rosh* (head), meaning the connection with the "head of the congregation," "your heads, your tribes," for through the connection with "your heads, your tribes," even "your wood-chopper and your water-drawer" will arrive at the revelation of the name Hashem. But there must be the connection, and not to be separated, Heaven forbid, from the bequeather and the head, as mentioned above regarding *teshuvah*, which is like the son who cannot bear that his father says he is not his father, and wants to be connected to him. Through this, "and you shall know that I am Hashem," that you will be connected (*daas* is a term for connection) to the name Hashem from above, the category of "He was, He is, and He will be" as one, the category of the Infinite, all of which comes through *teshuvah*.
